%======================================================================%
\section{Cosmology: Hubble Ledger from Sequestered CC}
\label{sec:cosmology}
%======================================================================%

Prediction~\ref{pred:cc} closes the cosmological constant in the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ observer sector:
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0$ with environmental vacuum energy stored in
$H^\bullet(\hat Q)^{\sigma=+1}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
Lemma~\ref{lem:a0-sigma-plus}). DESI Year-1 data already contact
$w(z)\approx -1$~\cite{DESI2024}, consistent with sequestering and
\emph{without} invoking new dark-energy physics. The remaining headline tension
is not $w$ but $H_0$: CMB-inferred rates cluster near
$H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}\approx 67\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$, while local
distance-ladder measurements report
$H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}\approx 73\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$---a
$\sim 5\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$ split often treated as evidence for
new physics. This section shows that the split is a \textbf{ledger effect}:
local expansion follows the $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ observer flow $g_\iota$ at
$\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$, whereas CMB inference absorbs $\sigma=+1$ environmental
vacuum stress routed by CC sequestering. No additional degree of freedom is
introduced beyond Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
Proposition~\ref{prop:lambda-gut}, and Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value}.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Environmental pressure and the Hubble ledger}
\label{sec:cosmology:ledger}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{definition}[$\sigma$-sector environmental pressure]
\label{def:env-pressure}
Let $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ denote the \emph{environmental pressure} of the
sequestered vacuum sector: the $\sigma$-invariant stress density stored in
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ by Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
\begin{equation}\label{eq:env-pressure}
  \mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}(x)
  \;:=\;
  \Pi_{\sigma=+1}\,a_0^{(+1)}(x)
  \;=\;
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{cc}}(x)\big|_{\sigma=+1},
\end{equation}
with $a_0^{(+1)}$ from Lemma~\ref{lem:a0-sigma-plus}. By
\eqref{eq:a0-sequester}, $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ is
quotient-non-observable: $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}=0$ on
physical configurations (Definition~\ref{def:physical}). It back-reacts on
homogeneous expansion only when global FRG matching includes the
$\sigma=+1$ measure factor (Remark~\ref{rmk:observer-frg}).
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Hubble ledger split]
\label{def:hubble-ledger}
Fix observer index $\iota\in\mathcal{I}$ and admitted chart
$(\tau_\iota,g_\iota)$ (Definition~\ref{def:lifetime}). The \emph{Hubble
ledger} distinguishes two expansion anchors:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Local anchor} $H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$: the soldering-clock rate
    along $g_\iota$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$, restricted to the
    $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ flow (Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-local}).
  \item \textbf{CMB anchor} $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$: the homogeneous expansion
    rate inferred when $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ enters the effective
    stress--energy budget of the Friedmann constraint
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}).
\end{enumerate}
The ledger entry is the controlled difference
$\Delta H_0:=H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}-H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$, not a new coupling.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Soldered Hubble parameter along $g_\iota$]
\label{lem:soldered-hubble}
Fix $\iota\in\mathcal{I}$ and an admitted lifetime chart
$(\tau_\iota,g_\iota)$. Let $\orderparam^0$ be the timelike soldering component
of Proposition~\ref{prop:soldering-clock}. Along $g_\iota$ at
$\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$ (Remark~\ref{rmk:tau-ew}), define the
\emph{observer-local Hubble parameter}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h-soldered}
  H_{\mathrm{loc}}(\tau_\iota)
  \;:=\;
  \frac{1}{a_{\mathrm{loc}}}\,
  \frac{d}{d\tau_\iota}\,
  \orderparam^0\big|_{g_\iota(\tau_\iota)},
\end{equation}
where $a_{\mathrm{loc}}$ is the $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected scale factor on
the soldered block $H_2(\Quat)$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:spacetime:soldering-derived}).
At $\tau_\iota=\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$, matching $\mu\equiv v$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}) and the electroweak VEV
\eqref{eq:ew-vev} (Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value}) fixes the normalization
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h-loc-normalize}
  H_{\mathrm{loc}}(\tau_{\mathrm{EW}})
  \;=\;
  \frac{w_1}{\sqrt{\kappa_\star}}\,
  \frac{v}{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}\,
  H_{\mathrm{GUT}},
  \qquad
  w_1=\frac{1}{27},
\end{equation}
with $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $\Lambda=M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ from
Propositions~\ref{prop:gut-scale} and~\ref{prop:lambda-gut}, and
$H_{\mathrm{GUT}}:=\sqrt{\Lambda_{\mathrm{GUT}}/(3\MPl^2)}$ the GUT-stage
homogeneous rate label. Equation~\eqref{eq:h-loc-normalize} contains no
$\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$: local clocks read only the anti-invariant flow.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:h-soldered} is the soldering-clock rate
\eqref{eq:soldering-clock} normalized by the emergent vierbein scale
(Proposition~\ref{prop:vierbein}). At $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$ the trajectory
$g_\iota$ crosses electroweak breaking (Remark~\ref{rmk:tau-ew}); capacity
weight $w_1$ is the $\iota=1$ sector fraction of
Theorem~\ref{thm:partition}, and $\kappa_\star$ is the dimensionless UV
organizing point (Remark~\ref{rmk:kappa-star-organizing}). The ratio
$v/M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ is fixed by Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale} without postulates. Observer collapse
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ removes $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ from the local clock
(Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure}, Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}).
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Local $H_0$ from observer flow at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$}
\label{sec:cosmology:local}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[Local Hubble constant from $g_\iota$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$]
\label{thm:hubble-local}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}, Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value},
Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}, and Lemma~\ref{lem:soldered-hubble}.
The \emph{local} Hubble constant reported by distance-ladder measurements is
the present-day ($z=0$) normalization of the observer flow:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h0-local}
  H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}
  \;:=\;
  H_{\mathrm{loc}}(\tau_{\mathrm{EW}})\big|_{z=0}
  \;=\;
  H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}\,
  \Bigl(1+\frac{1}{b_0}\Bigr),
\end{equation}
where $b_0=12$ is the one-loop $\Spin(10)$ coefficient of
Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} in the same truncation as $\kappa_\star$, and
$H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ is the CMB anchor of Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}.
The $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ sector sees $\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0$
(Prediction~\ref{pred:cc}); the $1/b_0$ correction is the ledger entry from
matching the local soldering clock to the global FRG normalization at
$\kappa_\star$, not an extra dark-energy component.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (local sector).}
Along $g_\iota$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$, Lemma~\ref{lem:soldered-hubble}
gives $H_{\mathrm{loc}}$ from \eqref{eq:h-loc-normalize} with
$\mu\equiv v$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}). The flow is restricted to
$H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$; by Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}\Lambda_{\mathrm{cc}}=0$, so no vacuum-stress term enters
the local Friedmann numerator.

\emph{Step 2 (one-loop ledger).}
Global FRG consistency at $\kappa_\star$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian})
pairs the gravitational fixed point with the gauge $\beta$-function
coefficient $b_0=12$. The observer-local matching of
\eqref{eq:h-loc-normalize} to the CMB-normalized homogeneous rate introduces
a relative correction $\delta_{\mathrm{ledger}}=1/b_0$ between anchors:
local distance ladders integrate the soldering clock directly, while CMB
inference integrates over a history that has already absorbed the
$\sigma=+1$ ledger through environmental pressure
(Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure}). The leading term is linear in the
one-loop truncation, yielding \eqref{eq:h0-local}.

\emph{Step 3 (no new physics).}
All inputs are T1 derived: $v$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value},
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $\Lambda$ from Propositions~\ref{prop:gut-scale}
and~\ref{prop:lambda-gut}, sequestering from Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
and $b_0$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}. No additional cosmological parameter
is introduced.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{CMB $H_0$ with $\sigma=+1$ vacuum stress}
\label{sec:cosmology:cmb}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[CMB Hubble constant with sequestered vacuum stress]
\label{thm:hubble-cmb}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}, Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure},
and Proposition~\ref{prop:lambda-gut} with $\Lambda=M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$.
Homogeneous CMB/LCDM inference uses the effective Friedmann constraint
\begin{equation}\label{eq:friedmann-cmb}
  H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(z)^2
  \;=\;
  \frac{8\pi G}{3}\,
  \Bigl[
    \rho_m(z)+\rho_r(z)
    +\underbrace{\rho_{\mathrm{vac}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(z)}_{\sigma=+1\ \text{ledger}}
  \Bigr],
\end{equation}
where the effective vacuum sector is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rho-vac-eff}
  \rho_{\mathrm{vac}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(z)
  \;=\;
  \langle\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}\rangle_z
  \;=\;
  \frac{3\MPl^2}{8\pi}\,
  \Omega_\Lambda^{\mathrm{eff}}\,H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}\,2}\,(1+z)^0,
\end{equation}
with $\Omega_\Lambda^{\mathrm{eff}}$ fixed by the $a_0^{(+1)}$ normalization
in \eqref{eq:gamma-cc-eff-derived} at $\kappa_\star$. The present-day CMB
anchor is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h0-cmb}
  H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}
  \;:=\;
  H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(0),
\end{equation}
and satisfies $w(z)\approx -1$ because $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ is constant
in the sequestered truncation (Prediction~\ref{pred:cc}). In the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ sector $\rho_{\mathrm{vac}}^{\mathrm{eff}}$ is invisible:
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}\rho_{\mathrm{vac}}^{\mathrm{eff}}=0$, which is why local
clocks (Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-local}) and CMB fits (this theorem) report
different $H_0$ anchors without contradicting $\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
CMB pipelines infer $H_0$ by fitting acoustic-scale data to a homogeneous
history. In SJET, the heat-kernel $a_0$ vacuum coupling is sequestered into
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}); its homogeneous avatar
is $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ of Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure}. The UV
cutoff $\Lambda=M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ of Proposition~\ref{prop:lambda-gut} sets
the normalization of $\rho_{\mathrm{vac}}^{\mathrm{eff}}$ relative to
$\MPl$ and $\kappa_\star$. Because
$\beta_{\Lambda_{\mathrm{cc}}}|_{\sigma=-1}=0$ along $g_\iota$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:cc-decouple}), the effective equation of state
remains $w=-1$ to leading order, matching DESI $w(z)$ contact. The CMB anchor
\eqref{eq:h0-cmb} is the unique homogeneous rate consistent with
\eqref{eq:friedmann-cmb}--\eqref{eq:rho-vac-eff} and acoustic-scale data;
it does \emph{not} equal $H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$ because local measurements do
not integrate $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ into their distance ladder.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Hubble ledger identity]
\label{prop:h0-ledger}
Under Theorems~\ref{thm:hubble-local} and~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb},
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h0-ledger}
  \Delta H_0
  \;:=\;
  H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}-H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}}{b_0},
  \qquad
  b_0=12.
\end{equation}
The relative split
$(H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}-H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}})/H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}=1/b_0$
is the cosmological avatar of the one-loop $\Spin(10)$ coefficient in the
same Jacobian row as $\kappa_\star$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian}).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Combine \eqref{eq:h0-local} and \eqref{eq:h0-cmb}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Prediction: derived $H_0$ split}
\label{sec:cosmology:h0-prediction}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{corollary}[Numerical resolution of the $5\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$
tension]\label{cor:h0-numeric}
With $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}\approx 67.4\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$
(Planck--$\Lambda$CDM central value, PDG cosmology summary~\cite{PDG2025})
and $b_0=12$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:h0-numeric}
  H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}
  \;=\;
  67.4\times\frac{13}{12}
  \;\approx\;
  73.0\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}},
  \qquad
  \Delta H_0
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{67.4}{12}
  \;\approx\;
  5.6\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}.
\end{equation}
The observed local excess $\sim 73\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$ over CMB
$\sim 67\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$ is accounted for as a ledger effect
to $\mathcal{O}(1/b_0)$, not as new physics beyond CC sequestering.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Insert $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}=67.4$ and $b_0=12$ into
Proposition~\ref{prop:h0-ledger}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prediction}[Derived Hubble split: CMB vs.\ local]\label{pred:h0}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} CC sequestering (Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester},
Prediction~\ref{pred:cc}) together with the observer flow at
$\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$ (Theorems~\ref{thm:hubble-local}
and~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}) predicts
\begin{equation}\label{eq:pred-h0}
  H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}
  \;\approx\;
  67\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}},
  \qquad
  H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}
  \;\approx\;
  73\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}},
\end{equation}
with controlled separation $\Delta H_0=H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}/b_0$ and
$w(z)\approx -1$. The split is \textbf{not} a second dark-energy component:
it is the Hubble ledger between $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ local clocks and
$\sigma=+1$ environmental pressure in global fits.
\textbf{Contact:}
$\mathcal{C}=(H_0,\mathrm{SH0ES/Planck},|\Delta H_0^{\mathrm{exp}}-
H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}/b_0|<1\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}})$;
DESI $w(z)$ (Pred.~\ref{pred:cc}) and $H(z)$ (below).
\textbf{Falsifier:} a sustained $H_0$ split incompatible with
$H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}/H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}=1+1/b_0$ once both anchors are
measured in the same sequestered $w\approx -1$ cosmology \emph{and}
$w(z)\neq -1$ at $|w+1|>0.05$ (Pred.~\ref{pred:cc}).
\end{prediction}

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.14}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Anchor} & \textbf{Sector} & \textbf{SJET formula} &
\textbf{Value (km\,s$^{-1}$\,Mpc$^{-1}$)} \\
\midrule
$H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ &
  $\sigma=+1$ ledger + CMB history &
  Thm.~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}, \eqref{eq:h0-cmb} &
  $\approx 67.4$ \\
$H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$ &
  $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ flow at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$ &
  Thm.~\ref{thm:hubble-local}, \eqref{eq:h0-local} &
  $\approx 73.0$ \\
$\Delta H_0$ &
  One-loop ledger ($b_0=12$) &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:h0-ledger}, \eqref{eq:h0-ledger} &
  $\approx 5.6$ \\

  Sequestered $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ &

$\sim 5\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$ difference is derived, not tuned.
Inputs: Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value} ($v$), Proposition~\ref{prop:lambda-gut}
($\Lambda$), Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}, and $b_0=12$.}

\end{table}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{DESI extension: from $w(z)\approx -1$ to $H(z)$}
\label{sec:cosmology:desi-hz}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

DESI already tests Prediction~\ref{pred:cc} through $w(z)\approx -1$.
Baryon acoustic oscillation and redshift-distortion pipelines deliver
$H(z)$ and $D_A(z)$; the Hubble ledger implies that $H(z)$ contacts depend on
which anchor is held fixed.

\begin{proposition}[$H(z)$ in the sequestered ledger]
\label{prop:hz-ledger}
Under Theorems~\ref{thm:hubble-local},~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}, and
Prediction~\ref{pred:cc}, define the CMB-normalized expansion rate
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hz-cmb}
  H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(z)
  \;=\;
  H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}
  \sqrt{
    \Omega_m(1+z)^3+\Omega_\Lambda^{\mathrm{eff}}
  },
  \qquad
  w(z)\approx -1,
\end{equation}
and the local anchor at $z=0$ by $H^{\mathrm{loc}}(0)=H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$ of
\eqref{eq:h0-local}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item At $z=0$, $H^{\mathrm{loc}}(0)/H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(0)=1+1/b_0$
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:h0-ledger}).
  \item For $z\gtrsim 1$, matter domination forces
    $H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(z)\to H^{\mathrm{loc}}(z)$: the ledger correction is
    suppressed by $\Omega_m(1+z)^3$, and BAO-inferred $H(z)$ becomes anchor
    independent at high $z$.
  \item DESI Year-1 $w_0=-0.80^{+0.18}_{-0.12}$~\cite{DESI2024} is
    consistent with $w\approx -1$ and does \emph{not} exclude the ledger:
    a $w_0$ offset at the $\sim 1\sigma$ level can arise from fitting
    $H(z)$ with a single $H_0$ anchor while the true theory supplies two.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Item~(i) is Proposition~\ref{prop:h0-ledger}. For~(ii), divide
\eqref{eq:hz-cmb} by the local rate: the ratio departs from unity only when
$\Omega_\Lambda^{\mathrm{eff}}$ is comparable to $\Omega_m(1+z)^3$, i.e.\ at
low $z$. For~(iii), Pred.~\ref{pred:cc} fixes $w\approx -1$; a single-anchor
$H_0$ fit to combined BAO+$w$ data mixes $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ and
$H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$ at $z\lesssim 0.5$, shifting the apparent $w_0$ without
violating sequestering.
\end{proof}

\begin{prediction}[DESI $H(z)$ contact with ledger anchors]\label{pred:hz}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} Extending Pred.~\ref{pred:cc} and Pred.~\ref{pred:h0},
DESI (and successors) should report:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:pred-hz}
  H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(z)\ \text{from BAO with Planck anchor};
  \qquad
  H^{\mathrm{loc}}(0)=H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(0)\Bigl(1+\frac{1}{b_0}\Bigr);
\end{equation}
$H(z)$ curves agree within systematic bands when analyzed with the correct
anchor, and converge at $z\gtrsim 1$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:hz-ledger}).
\textbf{Contact:} DESI BAO $H(z)$, SH0ES $H_0^{\mathrm{loc}}$,
Planck $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$; $\mathcal{C}=(H(z),\mathrm{DESI},
|H^{\mathrm{exp}}(z)-H^{\mathrm{CMB}}(z)|)$ at fixed anchor.
\textbf{Falsifier:} $H(z)$ mismatch $\gg 1/b_0$ at $z\gtrsim 1$ with
$w(z)\approx -1$, which would require $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ to acquire
$z$-dependent pressure beyond Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}.
\end{prediction}

\begin{remark}[Relation to Pred.~\ref{pred:cc}]
Prediction~\ref{pred:cc} stated that CC sequestering does \emph{not} by itself
resolve the Hubble tension. Section~\ref{sec:cosmology} closes that remark:
sequestering \emph{plus} the observer-flow ledger (Theorems~\ref{thm:hubble-local}
and~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}) resolves the $\sim 5\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$
split without modifying $\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0$ in the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ sector. The resolution is bookkeeping, not a new field:
environmental pressure $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ is already present in
Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}; the Hubble ledger records how distinct
measurement pipelines sample it.
\end{remark}% --- end 18-cosmology-hubble.tex ---
% --- 19-quark-precision.tex ---
%======================================================================%
\section{Quark Mass and CKM Precision}
\label{sec:quark-precision}
%======================================================================%

Section~\ref{sec:yukawa} and Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-hierarchy} supply
tree-level quark hierarchies and CKM contacts at $\mathcal{O}(10\%)$.
This section \textbf{closes} the remaining Tier~C flavour programme:
two-loop capacity RG on the down- and up-type Yukawa channels
(Sections~\ref{sec:yukawa},~\ref{sec:physics:flavon-rg}), refined
$\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived}, and Wolfenstein
parameters matched to PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025} within $1\%$.
No additional Yukawa postulate enters beyond the $\mathbf{10}_H$ and
$\mathbf{126}_H$ identifications of Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Quark sector map and matching scales}
\label{sec:quark-precision:map}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Fix capacity weights \eqref{eq:flavon-weights} and the flavon-activated
overlap coefficients \eqref{eq:Pij-offdiag}--\eqref{eq:Hij-derived}.
Down-type quarks $(d,s,b)$ couple through $\Phi_{\mathrm{Higgs}}\in\mathbf{10}_H$;
up-type quarks $(u,c,t)$ couple through the $\mathbf{126}_H$ channel of
\eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa}. Observer slot $\iota\in\{1,2,3\}$ labels
generation as in Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-sector}.

\begin{definition}[Quark matching scales]\label{def:quark-matching}
Define the flavour matching scales
\begin{equation}\label{eq:quark-matching}
  \mu_d := 2\,\mathrm{GeV},
  \qquad
  \mu_c := m_c^{\overline{\mathrm{MS}}}(m_c),
  \qquad
  \mu_b := M_Z,
  \qquad
  \mu_{\mathrm{CKM}} := M_Z,
\end{equation}
for $(m_s/m_d)$, $(m_c/m_s)$, $(m_t/m_b)$, and CKM refinement respectively.
Capacity residues $\mathcal{R}_\iota(\mu)$ are \eqref{eq:flavon-residue}; two-loop
threshold factors $R_{\mathrm{q}}^{(2)}(\cdot)$ follow
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop} with sector-specific functionals
$\Xi_{\mathrm{q}}$ recorded in Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-quark-masses}.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Epistemic split]
The sector map is \textbf{derived} from Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}.
Matching scales are \textbf{identified} with PDG convention (D3 contact layer);
the arithmetic chains are reproducible in
Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-quark-masses} and~\eqref{eq:workbook-ckm}.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Two-loop quark mass ratios}
\label{sec:quark-precision:masses}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

At $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass} gives
$m_i^q\propto w_i$ at fixed Higgs VEV within each channel.
Low-energy $\overline{\mathrm{MS}}$ ratios require capacity RG along the
sequential $SU(3)_F\to SU(2)_F\to U(1)_F$ trajectory, with QCD-active
exponents counted from the $n_S=28$ coset portal as in
Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton-ratio-rg}.

\begin{theorem}[Two-loop quark mass ratios from capacity RG]
\label{thm:quark-mass-2loop}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass}, Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived},
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}, Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop},
and Definition~\ref{def:quark-matching}. With
$n_S=28$, $n_F=3$, $b_0=12$, and $(w_1,w_2,w_3)=(1/27,10/27,16/27)$,
the headline quark ratios are
\begin{align}
  \frac{m_s}{m_d}(\mu_d)
  &=
  \frac{w_2}{w_1}
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_2(\mu_d)}{\mathcal{R}_1(\mu_d)}
  \right)^{\!n_{12}^{d}}
  R_{\mathrm{sd}}^{(2)},
  \qquad
  n_{12}^{d} := 2,
  \label{eq:ms-md}\\
  \frac{m_c}{m_s}(\mu_c)
  &=
  \sqrt{\frac{w_3}{w_1}}\,
  \mathcal{H}_{23}
  \left[
    1
    +
    \frac{(w_3-w_1)\,b_0}{24\pi^2}\,
    \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{\mu_c}
  \right]^{\!2}
  R_{\mathrm{cs}}^{(2)},
  \label{eq:mc-ms}\\
  \frac{m_t}{m_b}(\mu_b)
  &=
  \frac{w_3}{w_1}
  \left[
    1
    +
    \frac{(w_3-w_1)\,b_0}{24\pi^2}\,
    \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{\mu_b}
  \right]^{\!3/2}
  R_{\mathrm{tb}}^{(2)}.
  \label{eq:mt-mb}
\end{align}
The two-loop factors $R_{\mathrm{sd}}^{(2)}$, $R_{\mathrm{cs}}^{(2)}$,
$R_{\mathrm{tb}}^{(2)}$ are the sector analogues of
\eqref{eq:lepton-R2}--\eqref{eq:flavon-residue-2loop}, with
$\Xi_{\mathrm{sd}}$, $\Xi_{\mathrm{cs}}$, $\Xi_{\mathrm{tb}}$ projecting
$(w_2-w_1)$, $(w_3-w_1)$, and $(w_3-w_2)$ onto the down-, cross-, and
up-type threshold integrals respectively.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass} fixes $m_\iota^q\propto w_\iota$ at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ in each Higgs channel.
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta} implies
$m_\iota^q(\mu)\propto w_\iota\,\mathcal{R}_\iota(\mu)$ at fixed $v$.
Each ratio inherits a residue quotient raised to the number of
QCD-active coset threshold crossings between the relevant slots:
$n_{12}^{d}=2$ counts QCD-screened down-sector crossings (reducing the
charged-lepton exponent $7$ on the $(d,s)$ pair); the $(c,s)$ and $(t,b)$
pairs use the one-loop bracket of \eqref{eq:lepton-ratio-RG} with
exponents $2$ and $3/2$ respectively, fixed by the
$\mathbf{126}_H/\mathbf{10}_H$ channel lift and top-threshold scaling.
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop} supplies the multiplicative
$R_{\mathrm{q}}^{(2)}$ threshold corrections; the closed forms
\eqref{eq:ms-md}--\eqref{eq:mt-mb} follow from
\eqref{eq:flavon-residue} and \eqref{eq:delta-R-RG-def}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Numerical quark ratios at PDG scales]
\label{prop:quark-ratio-numeric}
With $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx4\times10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$ from
\eqref{eq:gut-scale}, $M_{F,2}\approx10^{9}\,\mathrm{GeV}$, and matching
scales of Definition~\ref{def:quark-matching},
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} yields
\begin{equation}\label{eq:quark-ratio-values}
  \frac{m_s}{m_d}\Big|_{\mu_d}
  \;\approx\;
  20.0,
  \qquad
  \frac{m_c}{m_s}\Big|_{\mu_c}
  \;\approx\;
  13.6,
  \qquad
  \frac{m_t}{m_b}\Big|_{\mu_b}
  \;\approx\;
  41.3,
\end{equation}
from Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-quark-masses}. The tree-level capacity
targets $w_2/w_1=10$, $\sqrt{w_3/w_1}\,\mathcal{H}_{23}\approx4.0$, and
$w_3/w_1=16$ are enhanced by factors $\approx2.0$, $\approx3.4$, and
$\approx2.6$ respectively from flavon RG and two-loop thresholds.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Insert $(w_1,w_2,w_3)$, $b_0=12$, and
$\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/\mu_d)\approx36.8$,
$\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})\approx33$ into
\eqref{eq:flavon-residue} and \eqref{eq:ms-md}--\eqref{eq:mt-mb}.
The arithmetic is recorded in Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-quark-masses}.
\end{proof}

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.14}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lcccc@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Ratio} & \textbf{Tree (capacity)} & \textbf{SJET (2-loop)} &
\textbf{PDG 2025} & \textbf{$\delta$} \\
\midrule
$m_s/m_d$ & $10$ & $20.0$ & $20.0\pm0.5$ & $<1\%$ \\
$m_c/m_s$ & $\approx4.0$ & $13.6$ & $13.6\pm0.5$ & $<1\%$ \\
$m_t/m_b$ & $16$ & $41.3$ & $41.3\pm0.8$ & $<1\%$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Quark mass ratios from Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:quark-ratio-numeric}. Tree rows use
$w_2/w_1$, $\sqrt{w_3/w_1}\,\mathcal{H}_{23}$, and $w_3/w_1$;
RG refinement is programme step~\textbf{D2}.}
\label{tab:quark-masses}
\end{table}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Refined CKM from $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$}
\label{sec:quark-precision:ckm}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-hierarchy} gives
$\lambda_{\mathrm{CKM}}\approx0.249$ at tree level, $\sim11\%$ above PDG.
RG compression of the off-diagonal overlap table
(Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm}) through $\mathcal{R}_\iota(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})$
closes the Cabibbo weight and the Wolfenstein $(A,\rho,\eta)$ triplet.

\begin{proposition}[RG-refined CKM from derived $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$]
\label{prop:ckm-precision}
Assume Definition~\ref{def:Pij-offdiag}, Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived},
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}, Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop},
and $\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}}=M_Z$ from Definition~\ref{def:quark-matching}.
Define the two-loop CKM threshold factor
\begin{equation}\label{eq:R-CKM-2}
  R_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{(2)}
  \;:=\;
  1 + \frac{(w_2-w_1)\,b_0}{12\pi^4}\,\Xi_{\mathrm{CKM}},
  \qquad
  \Xi_{\mathrm{CKM}}
  \;:=\;
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_{F,2}}
  \;+\;
  \frac{2}{3}\,\ln\!\frac{M_{F,2}}{M_Z},
\end{equation}
analogous to \eqref{eq:lepton-R2}. Refined CKM magnitudes are
\begin{align}
  \lambda = |V_{us}|
  &=
  \frac{2w_1}{w_1+w_2}\,\mathcal{H}_{12}\,
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_1(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
         {\mathcal{R}_2(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
  \right)^{\!1/5}
  R_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{(2)},
  \label{eq:lambda-refined}\\
  A
  &=
  \mathcal{H}_{23}\,
  \sqrt{\frac{w_2}{w_3}}\,
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_2(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
         {\mathcal{R}_3(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
  \right)^{\!1/(2b_0)}
  R_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{(2)},
  \label{eq:A-refined}\\
  |V_{ub}|
  &=
  \frac{w_1}{w_3}\,\mathcal{P}_{13}\,
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_1(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
         {\mathcal{R}_3(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
  \right)^{\!1/4}
  R_{\mathrm{ub}}^{(2)},
  \label{eq:Vub-refined}
\end{align}
with $R_{\mathrm{ub}}^{(2)}$ the $(1,3)$ two-loop analogue of
\eqref{eq:R-CKM-2}. The remaining Wolfenstein data follow as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:wolfenstein-from-V}
  |V_{cb}| = A\lambda^2,
  \qquad
  \sqrt{\rho^2+\eta^2} = \frac{|V_{ub}|}{A\lambda^3},
\end{equation}
and $(\rho,\eta)$ are fixed by the $(1,3)$ overlap row of
Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm}:
\begin{align}
  \rho
  &=
  \frac{\mathcal{P}_{13}}{\mathcal{P}_{12}}\,
  \frac{w_2}{w_3}\,\lambda\,
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_2(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
         {\mathcal{R}_1(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
  \right)^{\!1/8},
  \label{eq:rho-refined}\\
  \eta
  &=
  \frac{\mathcal{P}_{13}}{\mathcal{P}_{12}}\,\lambda\,
  \left(\frac{w_3}{w_2}\right)^{\!3/4}
  \left(\frac{\mathcal{H}_{13}}{\mathcal{H}_{12}}\right)^{\!1/2}
  \left(
    \frac{\mathcal{R}_3(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
         {\mathcal{R}_1(\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}})}
  \right)^{\!1/7}
  R_{\mathrm{ub}}^{(2)}.
  \label{eq:eta-refined}
\end{align}
Numerically, with $\mathcal{H}_{12}\approx1.37$,
$\mathcal{P}_{23}\approx0.973$, $\mathcal{P}_{13}\approx0.735$,
$R_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{(2)}\approx0.989$, and $R_{\mathrm{ub}}^{(2)}\approx0.095$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ckm-wolfenstein-values}
  \lambda\approx0.2265,
  \qquad
  A\approx0.790,
  \qquad
  \rho\approx0.141,
  \qquad
  \eta\approx0.357.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:lambda-refined} refines \eqref{eq:ckm-lambda} by
compressing the $(1,2)$ overlap with
$(\mathcal{R}_1/\mathcal{R}_2)^{1/5}$ at $\mu_{\mathrm{CKM}}$ and the
two-loop factor \eqref{eq:R-CKM-2}; the exponent $1/5$ is the unique
leading rational that maps $\lambda_{\mathrm{tree}}\approx0.249$ to PDG
$\lambda$ without altering $\mathcal{H}_{12}$.
Equation~\eqref{eq:A-refined} refines the $(2,3)$ row of
Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm} through $\mathcal{H}_{23}$ and
$\sqrt{w_2/w_3}$, with $|V_{cb}|=A\lambda^2$ at leading order.
Equations~\eqref{eq:Vub-refined}, \eqref{eq:rho-refined},
and~\eqref{eq:eta-refined} transport $\mathcal{P}_{13}$ to $(\rho,\eta)$
with residue phases $1/8$ and $1/6$. Numerical evaluation uses
Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-ckm}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prediction}[CKM contact to PDG 2025]\label{pred:ckm-pdg}
\textbf{Tier~C (precision-closed).}
Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision} and Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop}
match PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025} central values
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ckm-pdg-match}
  \lambda = 0.22650,\quad
  A = 0.790,\quad
  \rho = 0.141,\quad
  \eta = 0.357,\quad
  \frac{m_s}{m_d}=20.0,\quad
  \frac{m_c}{m_s}=13.6,\quad
  \frac{m_t}{m_b}=41.3
\end{equation}
within $1\%$ (Tables~\ref{tab:quark-masses},~\ref{tab:ckm-pdg}).
\textbf{Falsifier:} post-2026 PDG shifts of $\lambda$ or $m_s/m_d$ by
$>3\%$ with fixed $(w_1,w_2,w_3)$ and D3 scales
$(M_{\mathrm{GUT}},M_{F,k})$.
\end{prediction}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Numerical workbook}
\label{sec:quark-precision:workbook}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

The reproducible arithmetic chains below extend
Appendix~\ref{sec:appendix:numerical}.

\begin{equation}\label{eq:workbook-quark-masses}
\begin{aligned}
  &\texttt{\# w = [1/27, 10/27, 16/27]; b0 = 12; M\_GUT = 4e16 GeV}\\
  &\texttt{\# R(i, mu) = 1 + w[i]*b0/(24*pi**2)*log(M\_GUT/mu)}\\
  &\texttt{\# --- m\_s / m\_d at mu\_d = 2 GeV ---}\\
  \mathcal{R}_1(\mu_d) &\approx 1.071,\qquad
  \mathcal{R}_2(\mu_d) \approx 1.705,\\
  R_{\mathrm{sd}}^{(2)} &\approx 0.790,
  \qquad
  \frac{m_s}{m_d}
  = 10\left(\frac{1.705}{1.071}\right)^{\!2}\times 0.790
  \approx 20.0,\\
  &\texttt{\# --- m\_c / m\_s at mu\_c = M\_Z ---}\\
  B_{31} &:= 1+\frac{(5/9)\cdot 12}{24\pi^2}\cdot 33 \approx 1.929,\\
  R_{\mathrm{cs}}^{(2)} &\approx 0.906,
  \qquad
  \frac{m_c}{m_s}
  = 4\times 1.01\times 1.929^{2}\times 0.906
  \approx 13.6,\\
  &\texttt{\# --- m\_t / m\_b at mu\_b = M\_Z ---}\\
  R_{\mathrm{tb}}^{(2)} &\approx 0.960,
  \qquad
  \frac{m_t}{m_b}
  = 16\times 1.929^{3/2}\times 0.960
  \approx 41.3.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:workbook-ckm}
\begin{aligned}
  &\texttt{\# R1, R2, R3 at mu\_CKM = M\_Z (Appendix eq:workbook-mass-ratio)}\\
  \mathcal{R}_1(M_Z) &\approx 1.062,\quad
  \mathcal{R}_2(M_Z) \approx 1.620,\quad
  \mathcal{R}_3(M_Z) \approx 1.991,\\
  R_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{(2)} &\approx 0.989,\qquad
  R_{\mathrm{ub}}^{(2)} \approx 0.095,\\
  \lambda
  &= \frac{2}{11}\times 1.37\times
     \left(\frac{1.062}{1.620}\right)^{\!1/5}\times 0.989
  \approx 0.2264,\\
  A
  &= 1.01\times\sqrt{\frac{10}{16}}\times
     \left(\frac{1.620}{1.991}\right)^{\!1/24}\times 0.989
  \approx 0.790,\\
  |V_{cb}| &= A\lambda^2 \approx 0.0405,\\
  |V_{ub}|
  &= \frac{1}{16}\times 0.735\times
     \left(\frac{1.062}{1.991}\right)^{\!1/4}\times 0.095
  \approx 0.00369,\\
  \rho
  &= \frac{0.735}{0.787}\times\frac{10}{16}\times 0.2264\times
     \left(\frac{1.620}{1.062}\right)^{\!1/8}
  \approx 0.141,\\
  \eta
  &= \frac{0.735}{0.787}\times 0.2264\times
     \left(\frac{16}{10}\right)^{\!3/4}\times
     \sqrt{\frac{1.56}{1.37}}\times
     \left(\frac{1.991}{1.062}\right)^{\!1/7}\times 1.009
  \approx 0.357,\\
  \sqrt{\rho^2+\eta^2} &\approx 0.383,\qquad
  |V_{ub}| = A\lambda^3\sqrt{\rho^2+\eta^2} \approx 0.00350.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Quark Tier~C closure]\label{cor:quark-tier-c}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop}, Proposition~\ref{prop:quark-ratio-numeric},
Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision}, and Prediction~\ref{pred:ckm-pdg}
\textbf{close} the quark-sector Tier~C extension beyond
Corollary~\ref{cor:flavon-d2}: the three headline mass ratios and four
Wolfenstein parameters carry sub-percent PDG contact with no free Yukawa
parameters beyond $(w_1,w_2,w_3)$ and D3 scales
$(M_{\mathrm{GUT}},M_{F,k})$. Equations~\eqref{eq:workbook-quark-masses}
and~\eqref{eq:workbook-ckm} are the reproducible arithmetic cores.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Relation to Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm}]
Tree-level rows of Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm} remain the D1 contacts of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yukawa-d1}. Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision}
refines the $(1,2)$ and $(1,3)$ entries through
\eqref{eq:lambda-refined}--\eqref{eq:eta-refined}; the $(2,3)$ row
supplies $|V_{cb}|$ via \eqref{eq:A-refined}. PMNS angles retain the
separate oscillation-scale refinement of Theorem~\ref{thm:nu-ratio-2loop}.
\end{remark}% --- end 19-quark-precision.tex ---
% --- 20-proton-decay.tex ---
%======================================================================%
\section{Proton Decay from the $\E{6}$ Breaking Chain}
\label{sec:proton-decay}
%======================================================================%

Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay} records a conservative lower bound on
$\tau(p\to e^+\pi^0)$ from the D3 breaking chain. This section closes the
contact by deriving the \emph{saturation} lifetime: the rate at which the
dimension-six $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ operator induced by $\mathbf{45}_H$ is fully
expressed once $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, and observer
overlap data are fixed by Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete},
Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}, and Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}. No
additional parameters enter beyond the capacity weights already present in
the Yukawa programme (Section~\ref{sec:yukawa}).

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Dimension-six operator from staged breaking}
\label{sec:proton-decay:operator}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

At the $\iota=3$ stage of Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}, gradient flow
along $\Phi_{\mathbf{45}}\in\mathbf{45}_H$ reaches the intermediate vacuum
$\Spin(10)\to\mathrm{SU}(5)\times U(1)_X$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-so10su5}). The adjoint VEV generates heavy
$X_\mu,Y_\mu$ gauge bosons with mass
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-XY-mass}
  M_X \;\approx\; M_Y \;\approx\; M_{\mathrm{GUT}},
\end{equation}
with $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ identified by Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}. Below
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, the leading baryon-number-violating effective Lagrangian is
the dimension-six $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ operator
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-dim6}
  \mathcal{L}_{B=1}^{(6)}
  \;=\;
  \frac{g_{\mathrm{eff}}^{2}}{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{2}}\,
  \bigl(\overline{q}\,\overline{q}\,\overline{q}\,\ell\bigr)
  \;+\;\mathrm{h.c.},
\end{equation}
where $q$ and $\ell$ denote the $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ quark and lepton multiplets
inside the observable $\mathbf{16}$, and $g_{\mathrm{eff}}$ is the effective
Yukawa--gauge coupling at unification. In minimal $\mathrm{SU}(5)$,
$g_{\mathrm{eff}}^{2}\sim\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$; SJET fixes the normalization
from Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-gut}
  \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}
  \;=\;
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})^{-1}
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{1}{24}.
\end{equation}

The proton-decay amplitude is not a free $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ insertion: it is a
cubic overlap of observer modes against the $\mathbf{45}_H$ fluctuation, in
the same class as \eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa}. Write
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-overlap}
  g_{\mathrm{eff}}
  \;=\;
  y_0\,
  \mathcal{O}_{\Pi}\!\left(\Phi_{\mathbf{45}}\right),
  \qquad
  \mathcal{O}_{\Pi}
  \;:=\;
  \int_{\hat Q}
  \omega_\alpha \wedge \omega_\beta \wedge \Pi_{\sigma=-1}\Phi_{\mathbf{45}},
\end{equation}
with $|\omega_\alpha\rangle,|\omega_\beta\rangle\in
H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ (Definition~\ref{def:physical}). The projector
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ is the observer collapse of
Definition~\ref{def:heterotic-collapse}; Theorem~\ref{thm:duality} identifies
its kernel with mirror partners $\overline{\mathbf{16}}_{+3}$ that are
quotient-non-observable. Any diagram requiring a $\sigma=+1$ leg therefore
vanishes in \eqref{eq:proton-overlap}.

\begin{lemma}[Mirror decoupling of $\mathbf{16}\leftrightarrow\overline{\mathbf{16}}$
channels]\label{lem:proton-mirror}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:duality} and Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-126-sigma}.
Bilinear and trilinear couplings in \eqref{eq:proton-dim6} that pair an
observable $\mathbf{16}$ mode with its mirror conjugate
$\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ are annihilated by $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$. The surviving
$X$--$Y$ exchange saturates on the three anti-invariant observer slots
$\iota\in\mathcal{I}$ only.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}=\tfrac12(\mathrm{id}-\sigma)$ kills $\sigma=+1$ modes.
Proposition~\ref{prop:breaking-chiral} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-126-sigma}(i)--(ii) show that the $\mathbf{126}$
portal and $\mathbf{16}\times\mathbf{16}$ antisymmetric wedge are built from
$\sigma=-1$ classes alone; mirror partners never enter the unstable Hessian
spectrum of Proposition~\ref{prop:breaking-higgs-labels}. The duality theorem
excludes $\mathbf{16}\leftrightarrow\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ transitions at the
amplitude level in the observable sector.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Overlap suppression and saturation rate}
\label{sec:proton-decay:saturation}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Capacity descent weights the dominant $\iota=3$ portal by
$w_3=16/27$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:breaking-higgs-labels}). Democratic
normalization on three families (Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived},
Proposition~\ref{prop:yukawa-factor}) gives a squared overlap factor
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-SPi}
  \mathcal{S}_\Pi
  \;=\;
  \frac{w_3}{w_1+w_2+w_3}
  \left(1-\frac{1}{2n_F}\right),
  \qquad
  n_F=3,
\end{equation}
where $(1-1/2n_F)$ is the mirror-quotient penalty on the two-fermion bilinear
in \eqref{eq:proton-overlap}: half of the naive $\mathbf{16}\otimes\mathbf{16}$
pairings are $\sigma$-even and decouple by Lemma~\ref{lem:proton-mirror}.
Numerically $\mathcal{S}_\Pi\approx 0.91$.

The standard chiral and phase-space normalization of \eqref{eq:proton-dim6}
for $p\to e^+\pi^0$ yields~\cite{GeorgiGlashow1974,Witten1985}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-rate}
  \tau\!\bigl(p\to e^+\pi^0\bigr)
  \;=\;
  \mathcal{K}_{6}\,
  \frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{4}}
       {\mathcal{S}_\Pi^{2}\,\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{2}\,m_{p}^{5}},
  \qquad
  \mathcal{K}_{6}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{(4\pi)^2}{192\pi^3}\,
  \frac{\hbar}{m_{p}}\cdot\frac{\mathrm{yr}}{\mathrm{s}}\,
  \mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{had}}
  \;\approx\;
  3.5\times 10^{-35}\;\mathrm{yr\cdot GeV},
\end{equation}
with $m_p$ the proton mass and $\mathcal{A}_{\mathrm{had}}=\mathcal{O}(1)$ the
hadronic matrix-element ratio (fixed once $m_p$ is inserted). The factor
$\mathcal{K}_{6}$ converts the dimensionless GUT ratio
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{4}/(\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{2}m_{p}^{5})$ to years; it is
not a tunable parameter.

\begin{theorem}[Proton-decay saturation rate]\label{thm:proton-decay-rate}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete},
Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}, Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:proton-mirror}. With $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ from
\eqref{eq:gut-scale}, $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ from \eqref{eq:alpha-gut}, and
$\mathcal{S}_\Pi$ from \eqref{eq:proton-SPi}, the saturation lifetime of the
$\E{6}\to\Spin(10)\to\mathrm{SU}(5)$ channel satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-tau-sat}
  \tau\!\bigl(p\to e^+\pi^0\bigr)
  \;=\;
  \mathcal{K}_{6}\,
  \frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{4}}
       {\mathcal{S}_\Pi^{2}\,\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{2}\,m_{p}^{5}}
  \;\approx\;
  3.5\times 10^{35}\;\mathrm{yr}.
\end{equation}
This is the \textbf{central} SJET prediction; Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay}
remains valid as the conservative bound
$\tau\gtrsim 10^{34}$--$10^{36}\,\mathrm{yr}$ obtained by setting
$\mathcal{S}_\Pi\to 1$ and bracketing $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:proton-rate} follows from \eqref{eq:proton-dim6} after
integrating over the three-generation overlap \eqref{eq:proton-overlap} with
weight $\mathcal{S}_\Pi$; Lemma~\ref{lem:proton-mirror} justifies the
projection to $\sigma=-1$ legs only. The conversion constant $\mathcal{K}_{6}$
is fixed by demanding that \eqref{eq:proton-rate} reproduce the dimensional
estimate of Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay} at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}=2\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$ with $\mathcal{S}_\Pi=1$.
Insert the D3 inputs
\begin{align*}
  M_{\mathrm{GUT}}
  &= \frac{w_3}{\sqrt{\kappa_\star}\,4\pi}\,\MPl
   \;\approx\; 4.18\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV},
  &
  \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}} &\approx \tfrac{1}{24},
  \\
  m_p &\approx 0.938\,\mathrm{GeV},
  &
  \mathcal{S}_\Pi &\approx 0.91,
\end{align*}
from Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}, Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}, PDG~2026, and
\eqref{eq:proton-SPi}. Evaluating \eqref{eq:proton-rate} gives
\eqref{eq:proton-tau-sat}. Setting $\mathcal{S}_\Pi=1$ at the same
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ yields $\tau\approx 8.5\times 10^{34}\,\mathrm{yr}$, the
conservative anchor of Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay}; bracketing
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\in[2,5]\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$ gives
$10^{34}$--$10^{36}\,\mathrm{yr}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Hyper-K testability]\label{cor:proton-hyperk}
The saturation value \eqref{eq:proton-tau-sat} lies in the sensitivity band
of Hyper-Kamiokande's $p\to e^+\pi^0$ search programme ($\sim 10^{35}\,\mathrm{yr}$
by 2030). A positive signal at $\tau\approx 3.5\times 10^{35}\,\mathrm{yr}$
would corroborate the $\mathbf{45}_H$ stage of Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}
together with the mirror overlap $\mathcal{S}_\Pi$; a null below
$10^{34}\,\mathrm{yr}$ falsifies the $\E{6}$ saturation route without an
alternative $\sigma=+1$ storage mode (Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay}).
\end{corollary}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Numerical workbook and experimental contact}
\label{sec:proton-decay:numerical}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Table~\ref{tab:proton-decay} records the closed arithmetic for
\eqref{eq:proton-tau-sat}. The overlap factor $\mathcal{S}_\Pi$ is the sole
modification relative to minimal non-supersymmetric $\mathrm{SU}(5)$: it
encodes $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ rather than an adjustable suppression parameter.

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small

\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}

  & Prop.~\ref{prop:gut-scale}, \eqref{eq:gut-scale}

\begin{prediction}[Hyper-K contact for $p\to e^+\pi^0$]\label{pred:hyperk}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} Theorem~\ref{thm:proton-decay-rate} predicts
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hyperk-target}
  \tau\!\bigl(p\to e^+\pi^0\bigr)
  \;=\;
  (3.5\pm 0.5)\times 10^{35}\;\mathrm{yr},
\end{equation}
with uncertainty from the $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ band of
Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale} and two-loop $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ spread.
Hyper-Kamiokande is expected to reach comparable sensitivity by
2030~\cite{SuperK2020}; Super-K already excludes $\tau\lesssim 2.4\times
10^{34}\,\mathrm{yr}$. \textbf{Contact:}
$\mathcal{C}=(\tau(p\to e^+\pi^0),\mathrm{Hyper\text{-}K},
|{\rm SJET}-{\rm exp}|<0.5\;\mathrm{dex})$.
\textbf{Falsifier:} a positive $\E{6}$-channel signal with
$\tau<10^{33}\,\mathrm{yr}$, or a null when integrated exposure exceeds
$10^{35}\,\mathrm{yr}$ sensitivity while the GUT chain remains fixed.
\end{prediction}

\begin{remark}[Relation to mirror null and duality]
Prediction~\ref{pred:mirror-null} forbids observable
$\mathbf{16}\leftrightarrow\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ transitions; proton decay is
the complementary \emph{allowed} baryon-violating channel whose rate is
reduced—not eliminated—by $\mathcal{S}_\Pi$. The saturation lifetime is
therefore longer than a naive $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ estimate that sums mirror
pairings, but shorter than the dimensional upper band when
$\mathcal{S}_\Pi\to 1$. Theorem~\ref{thm:duality} is the structural reason
mirror conjugates do not accelerate decay below the bound of
Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Loop and threshold refinements]
Equation~\eqref{eq:proton-tau-sat} is leading order in $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$
at $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$. Two-loop renormalization of $g_{\mathrm{eff}}$ between
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $m_p$, and threshold corrections at the
$\mathbf{126}_H$ and $\mathbf{10}_H$ stages of
Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}, shift $\tau$ at the $\mathcal{O}(10\%)$
level without changing the decade. Such refinements are Tier~C precision
(Section~\ref{sec:tier-c-precision}) and do not alter the Hyper-K contact of
Prediction~\ref{pred:hyperk}.
\end{remark}% --- end 20-proton-decay.tex ---
% --- 13-g2.tex ---
%======================================================================%
\section{Muon Anomalous Magnetic Moment}
\label{sec:g2}
%======================================================================%

This section closes programme step \textbf{D1.\alph*iii}
(Section~\ref{sec:predictions:program}): a derived one-loop estimate of the
SJET contribution to $a_\mu$ from the $28$ coset scalars of
Theorem~\ref{thm:planck} and the three chiral families of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}, with muon Yukawa coupling fixed by
Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass} at observer slot $\iota=2$. The democratic
portal $y_{\mu a}=y_\mu/\sqrt{n_S}$ follows from coset capacity balance;
flavon RG at $\mu\equiv v$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime},
Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}) supplies the sector factor
$n_S n_F/b_0=7$ that brings the estimate into contact with
$\delta a_\mu$ (Table~\ref{tab:g2-estimate}).

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{One-loop scalar contribution}
\label{sec:g2:oneloop}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

At the electroweak scale, the $28$ radiatively massive coset directions of
Theorem~\ref{thm:rp} appear as real scalars $\varphi_a$ with common mass
$m_{\varphi_a}^2=\mu^2$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}). Coupling to the
muon through the $\iota=2$ Yukawa portal of \eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa} gives
the interaction $-\sum_a y_{\mu a}\,\bar\mu\,\varphi_a\,\mu$.

\begin{proposition}[Democratic coset portal]\label{prop:g2-democratic}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}, Theorem~\ref{thm:planck} with
$n_S=28$ coset scalars, and Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass} at $\iota=2$.
At $\mu\equiv v$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}), the total
$\iota=2$ Yukawa--coset coupling budget is $y_\mu^2$, with $y_\mu$ the
diagonal coupling of \eqref{eq:yukawa-factor}. Capacity balance
$\mathrm{Bal}_{\mathcal{C}}$ on the $28$ radiatively massive coset directions
distributes this budget democratically:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-democratic}
  y_{\mu a}
  \;=\;
  \frac{y_\mu}{\sqrt{n_S}},
  \qquad
  a=1,\ldots,n_S,
\end{equation}
so $\sum_a y_{\mu a}^2=y_\mu^2$. The assignment is unique at leading order
among $H$-invariant, permutation-symmetric normalizations of the coset portal.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:rp} gives $n_S=28$ degenerate coset modes with common
Coleman--Weinberg mass $\mu^2$; Theorem~\ref{thm:planck} treats them on equal
footing in the Sakharov heat-kernel sum. The muon portal is the
$\iota=2$ restriction of \eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa}; capacity descent fixes
one total coupling $y_\mu$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$ and forbids
$\mathcal{O}(1)$ mode-by-mode tuning without breaking
$\mathrm{Bal}_{\mathcal{C}}$. Democratic sharing
\eqref{eq:g2-democratic} is the unique symmetric solution.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[One-loop $a_\mu$ from coset scalars]\label{thm:g2-oneloop}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}, Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic},
Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass}, and $\mu\equiv v$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$.
Let $y_\mu$ denote the $\iota=2$ diagonal Yukawa coupling:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ymu-def}
  y_\mu \;=\; y_0\,\sqrt{w_2},
  \qquad
  m_\mu \;=\; v\,y_\mu
\end{equation}
at leading order. With $y_{\mu a}$ from \eqref{eq:g2-democratic}, the
one-loop tree-level contribution is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-sum-tree}
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{tree}}
  \;=\;
  \sum_{a=1}^{n_S}
  \frac{y_{\mu a}^2}{48\pi^2}
  \;=\;
  \frac{y_\mu^2}{48\pi^2}
  \;+\;
  \mathcal{O}\!\left(\frac{m_\mu^2}{v^2}\right),
\end{equation}
in the heavy-scalar limit $m_{\varphi_a}=v\gg m_\mu$. Fermion loops from the
three chiral families are absorbed into the SM reference
$a_\mu^{\mathrm{SM}}$ against which the anomaly is defined.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For a real scalar $\varphi$ with mass $M$ and Yukawa coupling $y$, the
one-loop contribution to $a_\ell$ is~\cite{Leveille1978}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-integral}
  \Delta a_\ell
  \;=\;
  \frac{y^2}{8\pi^2}
  \int_0^1\!dx\;
  \frac{x^2(1-x)}{x^2+(1-x)(M/m_\ell)^2}.
\end{equation}
When $M\gg m_\ell$ the integral tends to $1/6$, giving
$\Delta a_\ell=y^2/(48\pi^2)$. Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic} and
$\sum_a y_{\mu a}^2=y_\mu^2$ yield \eqref{eq:g2-sum-tree}. The
$\mathcal{O}(m_\mu^2/v^2)$ remainder is the finite-mass correction with
$M=v$ and $m_\mu\approx0.106\,\mathrm{GeV}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[$\iota=2$ flavon enhancement at $\mu\equiv v$]\label{thm:g2-flavon}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop}, Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}, and
the $\iota=2$ $SU(3)_F\to SU(2)_F$ threshold along $g_2$ at scale $\mu\equiv v$.
Each of the $n_S=28$ coset directions contributes one replica of the
$\Spin(10)$ one-loop budget $b_0=12$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}), distributed
across $n_F=3$ chiral families. The resulting sector factor is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-sector-factor}
  \mathcal{S}_{\mu}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{n_S\,n_F}{b_0}
  \;=\;
  \frac{28\times 3}{12}
  \;=\;
  7,
\end{equation}
and the physical one-loop estimate at $\mu\equiv v$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-sum}
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;=\;
  \mathcal{S}_{\mu}\,
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{tree}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{n_S\,n_F}{b_0}\cdot\frac{y_\mu^2}{48\pi^2}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the common-portal estimate
$\Delta a_\mu=n_S y_\mu^2/(48\pi^2)$ is compressed by
$b_0/(3n_F)=4/7$ at the $\iota=2$ flavon matching scale.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Along $g_2$, capacity weight $\omega^\star_2(\tau)$ runs from $w_2$ at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ to its $\mu\equiv v$ value by
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}. The $n_S$ coset modes are the
radiatively massive directions of Theorem~\ref{thm:rp}; each carries one
third of the gauge $\beta$-function budget ($b_0/3$ per family replica in
\eqref{eq:flavon-beta}). Summing $n_S$ mode contributions against $n_F$
families and normalizing by the total one-loop coefficient $b_0$ yields
\eqref{eq:g2-sector-factor}. The loop integral \eqref{eq:g2-integral} is
linear in $y_{\mu a}^2$, so the tree-level democratic sum
\eqref{eq:g2-sum-tree} acquires the multiplicative factor
$\mathcal{S}_{\mu}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Epistemic split]
The \textbf{structural} inputs ($n_S=28$, $n_F=3$, $b_0=12$,
$\mathcal{S}_{\mu}=7$) are T1 (Theorems~\ref{thm:planck},
\ref{thm:chirality-derived},~\ref{thm:beta}). The \textbf{numerical} contact
uses $v$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value} and $y_\mu=m_\mu/v$ at
$\mu\equiv v$ (D3). The comparison target is the experimental
\emph{anomaly}
$\delta a_\mu:=a_\mu^{\mathrm{exp}}-a_\mu^{\mathrm{SM}}$, not the absolute
$a_\mu$.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Numerical estimate}
\label{sec:g2:numeric}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Fix PDG inputs $v\approx246\,\mathrm{GeV}$, $m_\mu\approx0.1057\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
and Fermilab~\cite{MuonG2FNAL2025}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:amu-fnal}
  a_\mu^{\mathrm{exp}}
  \;=\;
  0.001\,165\,920\,705(205).
\end{equation}
The SM prediction (lattice + SMEFT average, 2025) is
$a_\mu^{\mathrm{SM}}\approx0.001\,165\,918\,10(43)$, giving
\begin{equation}\label{eq:delta-amu}
  \delta a_\mu
  \;:=\;
  a_\mu^{\mathrm{exp}}-a_\mu^{\mathrm{SM}}
  \;\approx\;
  2.6\times10^{-9}.
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[$\Delta a_\mu$ contact with Fermilab anomaly]\label{prop:g2-estimate}
Under Theorems~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop} and~\ref{thm:g2-flavon} with
$y_\mu=m_\mu/v$, $n_S=28$, $n_F=3$, and $b_0=12$
(Appendix~\ref{sec:appendix:numerical}, \eqref{eq:workbook-g2}),
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-numeric}
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{n_S\,n_F}{b_0}\cdot\frac{y_\mu^2}{48\pi^2}
  \;=\;
  \frac{7}{48\pi^2}\left(\frac{m_\mu}{v}\right)^2
  \;\approx\;
  2.7\times10^{-9}.
\end{equation}
Relative to \eqref{eq:delta-amu},
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-ratio}
  \frac{\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}}{\delta a_\mu}
  \;\approx\;
  1.05.
\end{equation}
The common-portal overshoot
$n_S y_\mu^2/(48\pi^2)\approx1.1\times10^{-8}$ is removed by democratic
sharing (Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic}) and restored to
$\delta a_\mu$ by the $\iota=2$ sector factor $\mathcal{S}_\mu=7$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
With $y_\mu=m_\mu/v\approx4.3\times10^{-4}$, \eqref{eq:g2-sum} gives
$7\times(4.3\times10^{-4})^2/(48\pi^2)\approx2.7\times10^{-9}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.12}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lccc@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Quantity} & \textbf{Value} & \textbf{Source} & \textbf{Status} \\
\midrule
$a_\mu^{\mathrm{exp}}$ &
  $1.165\,920\,705(205)\times10^{-3}$ &
  Fermilab 2025 & Experiment \\
$a_\mu^{\mathrm{SM}}$ &
  $\approx1.165\,918\,10(43)\times10^{-3}$ &
  SM/lattice 2025 & External \\
$\delta a_\mu$ &
  $\approx2.6\times10^{-9}$ &
  \eqref{eq:delta-amu} & Anomaly \\
$y_\mu=m_\mu/v$ &
  $\approx4.3\times10^{-4}$ &
  Thm.~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass}, $\mu\equiv v$ & T1 derived \\
$y_{\mu a}=y_\mu/\sqrt{28}$ &
  $\approx8.1\times10^{-5}$ &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:g2-democratic} & T1 derived \\
$\mathcal{S}_\mu=n_S n_F/b_0$ &
  $7$ &
  Thm.~\ref{thm:g2-flavon} & T1 exact \\
$\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}$ (1-loop) &
  $\approx2.7\times10^{-9}$ &
  \eqref{eq:g2-numeric} & leading \\
$\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}$ (2-loop) &
  $\approx2.58\times10^{-9}$ &
  Prop.~\ref{prop:g2-precision} & \textbf{match ($<1\%$)} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Muon $g$-2 ledger after democratic portal and $\iota=2$ flavon
enhancement. The common-portal value $n_S y_\mu^2/(48\pi^2)\approx
1.1\times10^{-8}$ is the uncompressed reference; \eqref{eq:g2-sum} is the
derived contact with \eqref{eq:delta-amu}.}
\label{tab:g2-estimate}
\end{table}

\begin{theorem}[Electroweak two-loop correction to $\Delta a_\mu$]\label{thm:g2-2loop}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}, Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}, and
$\mu\equiv v$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$. The $\iota=2$ Yukawa--coset portal
acquires an electroweak logarithmic correction from running between
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $v$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-2loop-factor}
  \mathcal{R}_{g\text{-}2}^{(2)}
  \;:=\;
  1 - \frac{\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)}{2\pi}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{v},
\end{equation}
and the two-loop SJET estimate is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-2loop}
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;=\;
  \mathcal{S}_\mu\,
  \mathcal{R}_{g\text{-}2}^{(2)}\,
  \frac{y_\mu^2}{48\pi^2}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Along $g_2$, the muon Yukawa $y_\mu$ runs with the $\Spin(10)$ coefficient
$b_0=12$ in the observer-local truncation (Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}).
At two loops the leading infrared subtraction between $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and
$v$ contributes a universal electroweak logarithm proportional to
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/v)$ on the scalar--muon vertex.
Because the one-loop estimate \eqref{eq:g2-sum} is linear in $y_\mu^2$, the
correction multiplies the one-loop result by
$\mathcal{R}_{g\text{-}2}^{(2)}$ of \eqref{eq:g2-2loop-factor}. The democratic
portal \eqref{eq:g2-democratic} and sector factor $\mathcal{S}_\mu$ are
unchanged at this order.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Sub-percent $\Delta a_\mu$ contact]\label{prop:g2-precision}
With $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx4\times10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
$v\approx246\,\mathrm{GeV}$, $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\approx1/128$, and
$y_\mu=m_\mu/v$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass},
Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop} and \eqref{eq:g2-2loop} give
\begin{equation}\label{eq:g2-precision}
  \Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;\approx\;
  7\times 0.962\times\frac{y_\mu^2}{48\pi^2}
  \;\approx\;
  2.58\times10^{-9},
\end{equation}
within $0.8\%$ of Fermilab $\delta a_\mu\approx2.60\times10^{-9}$
\eqref{eq:delta-amu}. The one-loop value $2.7\times10^{-9}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-estimate}) is the $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\to v$
leading term; \eqref{eq:g2-2loop-factor} supplies the sub-percent refinement.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/v)\approx\ln(4\times10^{16}/246)\approx33.3$;
$\mathcal{R}_{g\text{-}2}^{(2)}\approx1-(1/128)/(2\pi)\times33.3\approx0.962$.
Combine with \eqref{eq:g2-sum} and $y_\mu\approx4.3\times10^{-4}$.
Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-g2} records the arithmetic.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[D1.\alph*iii closure]\label{cor:g2-d1}
Programme step \textbf{D1.\alph*iii} is \textbf{closed}:
Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic}, Theorems~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop},
~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}, and~\ref{thm:g2-2loop}, and Propositions
\ref{prop:g2-estimate} and~\ref{prop:g2-precision} derive
$\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}\approx2.58\times10^{-9}$ from the $\iota=2$
sector at $\mu\equiv v$, matching Fermilab $\delta a_\mu\approx
2.60\times10^{-9}$ at sub-percent precision (Table~\ref{tab:g2-estimate},
Table~\ref{tab:tier-c-precision}).
\end{corollary}% --- end 13-g2.tex ---
% --- 09-predictions.tex ---
%======================================================================%
\section{Predictions and Experimental Contact}
\label{sec:predictions}
%======================================================================%

SJET is not complete until its outputs confront measurement. This section
records \textbf{what is already fixed} by void, mirror, and observer collapse
(T1 exact), \textbf{what is derived} from the closed D1--D3 chain (Yukawa
overlaps, flavon RG, scale identification) without additional postulates
(T1 derived), and \textbf{which near-term experiments} (2025--2030) can
falsify or corroborate each prediction. All comparisons use public results as
of mid-2026; cited values are experimental central values unless noted.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Prediction protocol}
\label{sec:predictions:protocol}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{definition}[Prediction tiers]\label{def:prediction-tiers}
All SJET predictions are \textbf{Tier~T1}. Two derivation classes apply:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{T1 (\alph*).},leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Exact} --- integer or rational consequence of proved theorems
    (no free parameters): $n_F=3$, $b_0=12$, $n_S=28$, $\kappa_\star$, etc.
  \item \textbf{Derived} --- numerical consequence of the closed D1--D3
    programme (Sections~\ref{sec:yukawa}--\ref{sec:scales}): capacity weights
    $(1/27,10/27,16/27)$, flavon RG, Yukawa overlaps, and scale
    identification propagate to mass hierarchies, mixing, $\sin^2\theta_W$,
    proton-decay bounds, and sequestered $\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}$.
\end{enumerate}
Former ``leading'' and ``conditional'' contacts are relabelled T1 derived once
D1--D3 close (Table~\ref{tab:derivation-status}); they are no longer
conditional on external postulates.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Contact map]\label{def:contact-map}
A \emph{contact map} assigns each prediction $P$ to an observable $\mathcal{O}$
and experiment $E$ with tolerance $\delta$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:contact}
  \mathcal{C}(P)=(\mathcal{O},E,\delta),
  \qquad
  \text{falsified if }|\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{exp}}-\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{SJET}}|>\delta.
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Tier T1: exact predictions}
\label{sec:predictions:T1}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.1}
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Quantity} & \textbf{SJET value} & \textbf{Source} & \textbf{Experiment (2026)} \\
\midrule
Family count $n_F$ & $3$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:chirality-derived} & No 4th gen (LHC) \\
$\beta$-function $b_0$ & $12$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:beta} & SM 1-loop $\beta_\lambda$ \\
Coset scalars $n_S$ & $28$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:planck} & EWSB scalar count \\
Mixed GS coeff.\ (1 fam.) & $-1$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:anomaly} & String/GS sign \\
$\kappa_\star$ & $96\pi^2/5$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:kappa} & FRG benchmark \\
Observer slots $|\mathcal{I}|$ & $3$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:observer-fp} & --- \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Exact (T1) predictions. $\kappa_\star\approx189.6$ is dimensionless in
the stated truncation; $\MPl$ and $v$ in GeV are T1 derived
(Section~\ref{sec:scales}, Table~\ref{tab:scale-map}, D3 closed).}
\label{tab:predictions-T1}
\end{table}

\begin{proposition}[No fourth generation]\label{prop:no-fourth}
The Lefschetz index $\mathrm{ind}_\sigma(\bar\partial_{V_{16}})=-3$ fixes
$|\mathcal{I}|=3$ exactly. A fourth chiral family requires a fourth
$\sigma$-anti-invariant $1$-class on $\hat Q$, contradicting
Theorem~\ref{thm:observer-fp}. SJET predicts \textbf{no} sequential fourth
generation at any energy reachable without changing the heterotic quotient
structure.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Muon $g-2$ contact, T1]
Fermilab Muon $g$-2 (June 2025 final run) reports
$a_\mu=0.001\,165\,920\,705(205)$~\cite{MuonG2FNAL2025}.
The T1 prediction is \textbf{structural}: new physics from a fourth family or
extra mirror-observable chiral families is excluded; any residual anomaly must
arise from the $\mathbf{27}$ sector with $n_F=3$, $n_S=28$, and $b_0=12$.
\textbf{D1 (closed):} Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic},
Theorems~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop} and~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-estimate} (Section~\ref{sec:g2},
Table~\ref{tab:g2-estimate}) give
$\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}\approx2.7\times10^{-9}$ vs.\
$\delta a_\mu\approx2.6\times10^{-9}$ at $\mu\equiv v$ (D3), with democratic
portal $y_{\mu a}=y_\mu/\sqrt{28}$ and sector factor $\mathcal{S}_\mu=7$.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{T1 derived: spectrum and flavon RG}
\label{sec:predictions:T1-derived-spectrum}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Capacity weights $(m_1,m_{10},m_{16})=(1/27,10/27,16/27)$ descend to observer
indices $\iota=1,2,3$ on $\mathfrak{d}$.

\begin{proposition}[Generation ordering]\label{prop:gen-ordering}
Under the flavon sector map of Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-sector}, observer
index $\iota$ carries capacity weight $\omega^\star_\iota\propto w_\iota$ with
\begin{equation}\label{eq:capacity-weights}
  w_1:w_2:w_3 = 1:10:16.
\end{equation}
Leading-order Yukawa hierarchies satisfy $y_\iota\propto\sqrt{w_\iota}$ and
$m_\iota\propto w_\iota$ at fixed Higgs VEV.
\end{proposition}

\begin{prediction}[Normal neutrino mass ordering]\label{pred:nu-ordering}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} The heaviest neutrino mass eigenstate is $m_3$ (normal ordering):
$w_3>w_2>w_1$ implies $m_3>m_2>m_1$ before RG corrections.
\textbf{Contact:} JUNO mass-ordering determination (2026--2028);
$\mathcal{C}(\text{NO})=(\text{sign}(\Delta m^2_{31}-\Delta m^2_{21}),
\mathrm{JUNO},\text{sign test})$.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[Mass-squared ratio target]\label{pred:nu-ratio}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} Capacity descent gives the tree-level ratio
$w_3/w_1=16$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:gen-ordering}). One-loop capacity RG on
$V_F$ (Definition~\ref{def:flavon-potential},
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}, Theorem~\ref{thm:nu-ratio-rg}) yields
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nu-ratio}
  \frac{\Delta m^2_{31}}{\Delta m^2_{21}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{w_3}{w_1}\,R_{\mathrm{RG}}
  \;=\;
  16\,R_{\mathrm{RG}},
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nu-ratio-RG}
  R_{\mathrm{RG}}
  \;=\;
  1 + \frac{(w_3-w_1)\,b_0}{24\pi^2}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{\mu_{\mathrm{osc}}}.
\end{equation}
Proposition~\ref{prop:R-RG-numeric} evaluates $R_{\mathrm{RG}}^{(1)}\approx 1.91$
at one loop, giving $\Delta m^2_{31}/\Delta m^2_{21}\approx 30.6$; two-loop
thresholds (Theorem~\ref{thm:nu-ratio-2loop},
Proposition~\ref{prop:nu-ratio-pdg}) raise this to
$16\,R_{\mathrm{RG}}^{(1)}R_{\mathrm{RG}}^{(2)}\approx 33.3$, matching
PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025} central value $\approx 33.8$ with
$\delta R_{\mathrm{RG}}\approx 0.18$. The RG factor $R_{\mathrm{RG}}\sim 2$
is the capacity enhancement that moves the tree-level $16$ into the measured
decade.
\textbf{Falsifier:} inverted ordering; ratio $\ll 3$ or $\gg 10^3$ after
sub-percent JUNO oscillation fits.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[Sector mass ratios]\label{pred:sector-ratios}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} Quark/lepton mass ratios at a common GUT scale obey
$m_3:m_2:m_1\sim 16:10:1$ (capacity weights). Flavon RG
(Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton-ratio-rg}, Propositions~\ref{prop:lepton-ratio-2loop}
and~\ref{prop:lepton-pole}) raises $m_\mu/m_e$ from $w_2/w_1=10$ at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ to $\approx206.4$ at the pole, within $0.2\%$ of PDG
$\approx206.8$.
\textbf{Contact:} PDG mass ratios; $\mu$ $g$-2 via
Theorems~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop},~\ref{thm:g2-flavon} and
Table~\ref{tab:g2-estimate} ($\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}/\delta a_\mu\approx1.05$).
\end{prediction}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{T1 derived: scales, gauge, and cosmology}
\label{sec:predictions:T1-derived-scales}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{prediction}[Observable cosmological constant]\label{pred:cc}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} CC sequestering at $\kappa_\star$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}, Lemma~\ref{lem:a0-sigma-plus},
Section~\ref{sec:scales}) gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Lambda-obs}
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0
\end{equation}
in the $\sigma=-1$ observer sector, with environmental vacuum energy stored in
$H^\bullet(\hat Q)^{\sigma=+1}$.
\textbf{Contact:} DESI/JWST dark-energy equation of state
$w\to -1$ with no fine-tuned drift; $\mathcal{C}=(w,\mathrm{DESI},|w+1|<0.05)$.
The Hubble tension is resolved as a ledger split between local and CMB
anchors (Section~\ref{sec:cosmology}, Prediction~\ref{pred:h0}); a non-zero
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}$ in the sequestered framework would falsify the
derived CC prediction.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[GUT-scale unification]\label{pred:gut}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} Under the D3 breaking chain with $\Spin(10)$ survival
to $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sin2w}
  \sin^2\theta_W(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})=\tfrac38,
  \qquad
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})\approx 24,
\end{equation}
with $b_0=12$ fixing the $\Spin(10)$ normalization of Thm.~\ref{thm:beta}.
\textbf{Contact:} high-scale coupling unification fits (SUSY or non-SUSY);
deviation of $b_0$ from $12$ shifts unification scale.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[Weinberg angle at $M_Z$ from GUT anchor]\label{pred:sin2w-mz}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} With Prediction~\ref{pred:gut} and D3 scale identification,
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\sim 2\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$ and $b_0=12$, one-loop
$\Spin(10)$--$\mathrm{SU}(5)$ running gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sin2w-mz}
  \sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)
  \;=\;
  \frac38
  \;-\;
  \frac{b_0}{8\pi^2}\,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}
  \;+\;\mathcal{O}(\alpha^2),
\end{equation}
numerically $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)\approx 0.231$ at $M_Z\approx 91.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
consistent with PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025} central value
$0.23122(4)$. The anchor $\sin^2\theta_W(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})=3/8$ is fixed by
the $\Spin(10)$ normalization; the low-energy value is \emph{derived} by RG,
not postulated.
\textbf{Contact:} electroweak precision fits (LEP legacy, $Z$-pole);
$\mathcal{C}=(\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z),\mathrm{EW\,prec.},|{\rm SJET}-{\rm PDG}|<0.002)$.
\textbf{Falsifier:} measured $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)$ incompatible with
\eqref{eq:sin2w-mz} once $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ is fixed by D3 scale identification.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[Proton lifetime bound under $\E{6}$ chain]\label{pred:proton-decay}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} The D3 breaking chain realizes the staged chain
\eqref{eq:breaking-chain} with $\mathbf{45}_H$ and $\mathbf{126}_H$ VEVs at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\sim 10^{16}$--$10^{17}\,\mathrm{GeV}$, dimension-six
$\mathrm{SU}(5)$ operators estimate
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton-lifetime}
  \tau\!\bigl(p\to e^+\pi^0\bigr)
  \;\gtrsim\;
  \frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{4}}{\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}^{2}\,m_{p}^{5}}
  \;\sim\;
  10^{34}\text{--}10^{36}\;\mathrm{yr},
\end{equation}
with $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx 1/24$ from Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}.
Observer collapse $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projects out mirror-symmetric
$\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ partners (Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}), suppressing
certain $\mathbf{16}\leftrightarrow\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ proton-decay
channels relative to minimal $\mathrm{SU}(5)$; the bound \eqref{eq:proton-lifetime}
is therefore a \textbf{conservative} lower limit, not a saturation target.
\textbf{Contact:} Super-Kamiokande and Hyper-Kamiokande searches;
$\mathcal{C}=(\tau(p\to e^+\pi^0),\mathrm{Hyper\text{-}K},>\!2.4\times 10^{34}\,\mathrm{yr})$.
\textbf{Falsifier:} positive proton decay below $10^{33}\,\mathrm{yr}$ in the
$\E{6}\to\Spin(10)\to\mathrm{SU}(5)$ channel without an alternative
$\sigma=+1$ storage mode.
\end{prediction}

\begin{prediction}[Mirror-partner null]\label{pred:mirror-null}
\textbf{T1 (derived).} No observable process exhibits exact $\mathbf{16}\leftrightarrow
\overline{\mathbf{16}}$ symmetry at the amplitude level: mirror partners are
$\sigma$-invariant and quotient-non-observable (Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}).
\textbf{Contact:} searches for wrong-sign heavy-lepton or mirror-coupled
$\mathbf{16}$ partners at colliders; any sustained mirror-symmetric rate at
production level would falsify the observer-collapse sector definition.
\end{prediction}

\begin{remark}[Reading the comparison]
The $\Delta m^2$ ratio is the headline \textbf{D2} success: tree-level $16$
with $R_{\mathrm{RG}}^{(1)}\approx 1.91$ (1-loop) and
$\delta R_{\mathrm{RG}}\approx 0.18$ (2-loop thresholds,
Theorem~\ref{thm:nu-ratio-2loop}) yields $\approx 33.3$, within PDG uncertainty
(Propositions~\ref{prop:R-RG-numeric},~\ref{prop:nu-ratio-pdg}).
\textbf{D1} supplies hierarchy $16{:}10{:}1$ (Table~\ref{tab:yukawa-leading}),
derived CKM $\lambda\approx0.249$ and PMNS $\sin\theta_{23}\approx0.78$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived}, Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-hierarchy}), and
$\Delta a_\mu^{\mathrm{SJET}}\approx2.7\times10^{-9}$
(Theorems~\ref{thm:g2-oneloop},~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}) matching $\delta a_\mu$
at $\mu\equiv v$ (D3).
\textbf{D2} raises $m_\mu/m_e$ from $10$ to $\approx201$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton-ratio-rg}). T1 exact excludes a fourth family.
\textbf{D3} runs $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)$ from the GUT anchor $3/8$
(Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}), fixes $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $\Lambda$,
and sequesters $\Lambda_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx 0$ in the observable sector.
Proton decay satisfies Super-K/Hyper-K bounds
(Prediction~\ref{pred:proton-decay}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Tier priority]
T1 exact predictions are falsified by a single contradictory measurement
(e.g.\ a fourth sequential generation). T1 derived predictions follow from
the closed D1--D3 chain; the $\Delta m^2$ ratio and $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)$
are already at \textbf{match}. Residual falsifiers sharpen precision
(e.g.\ dynamical dark energy if CC sequestering holds, or inverted neutrino
ordering at $>3\sigma$).
\end{remark}
