\caption{Complete SM operator map: every term in
\eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian} is traced to the void--mirror pipeline through
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ on $\hat Q$. Tier labels follow
Definition~\ref{def:proof-tiers}.}
\label{tab:sm-operator-map}
\end{table}

\begin{theorem}[SM Lagrangian derived from observer collapse]
\label{thm:sm-lagrangian-derived}
Assume the master pipeline \eqref{eq:master-pipeline} with
$\mathfrak{U}^\star=\Climb^\infty(\Void)$, observer collapse
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ on $\hat Q$, and the staged vacuum of
Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}. Then the low-energy effective Lagrangian
on the soldered $d=4$ observer sector is \eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian}, with:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{(\roman*)},leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Gauge content} $G_{\mathrm{SM}}$ of
    \eqref{eq:sm-gauge-group} (Proposition~\ref{prop:sm-gauge-content}).
  \item \textbf{Three chiral generations} from
    $\dim H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}=3$
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}, Definition~\ref{def:sm-fields}).
  \item \textbf{One Higgs doublet} from $\Phi_{\mathbf{10}}\in\mathbf{10}_H$
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}, Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-complete}).
  \item \textbf{Covariant derivatives} \eqref{eq:sm-covariant} from the
    residual $G_{\mathrm{SM}}$ connection on $\hat Q$.
  \item \textbf{Yukawa matrices} from cubic overlap integrals
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-complete}, Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-yukawa-derived}).
  \item \textbf{Higgs potential} from $V_{\mathrm{eff}}$ along the
    $\iota=1$ unstable mode (Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-higgs-derived}).
  \item \textbf{Ghost sector} from $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ BRST gauge fixing
    (Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-ghost-derived}).
  \item \textbf{$\theta_{\mathrm{QCD}}=0$} in the observable sector
    (Proposition~\ref{prop:sm-theta-zero}, Theorem~\ref{thm:strong-cp}).
  \item \textbf{Anomaly cancellation} for the full three-family content
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:anomaly}).
\end{enumerate}
Every operator in Table~\ref{tab:sm-operator-map} appears in
\eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian} and is fixed by the pipeline
\eqref{eq:sm-pipeline}; no additional SM postulate is introduced.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (coset and breaking).}
Void and mirror fix $\mathfrak{U}^\star$ with $\E{6}$ coset data
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universe}). The action \eqref{eq:action} with coercive
$V$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:vacuum}) and Coleman--Weinberg lift
(Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-cw}) supplies $V_{\mathrm{eff}}$. Sequential
$\iota$-ordered gradient flow realizes \eqref{eq:breaking-chain}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}), fixing $G_{\mathrm{SM}}$ and the Higgs
labels $\mathbf{45}_H$, $\mathbf{126}_H$, $\mathbf{10}_H$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:breaking-higgs-labels}). This proves
\textbf{(i)} and the Higgs doublet of \textbf{(iii)}.

\emph{Step 2 (observer collapse and fermions).}
Definition~\ref{def:physical} restricts observables to
$H^\bullet(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$. Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}
gives three chiral $\mathbf{16}$s; standard $\mathrm{SU}(5)$ branching yields
the SM multiplet assignment of Definition~\ref{def:sm-fields}, proving
\textbf{(ii)}. OS reconstruction (Theorem~\ref{thm:qm-derived}) with soldering
(Theorem~\ref{thm:spacetime:soldering-derived}) supplies spinors and
$\slashed{D}$, proving \textbf{(iv)} and Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-fermion-derived}.

\emph{Step 3 (gauge and ghosts).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure} factorizes the gauge-fixed measure on
$\hat Q$. Quadratic gauge fluctuations about the stage~(4) vacuum yield
\eqref{eq:sm-gauge} (Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-gauge-derived}); BRST ghosts follow
from the adjoint Laplacian \eqref{eq:sm-ghost-operator}
(Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-ghost-derived}), proving \textbf{(vii)}.

\emph{Step 4 (Yukawa and Higgs).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete} defines cubic overlaps
\eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa}; Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-complete} evaluates the
full $3\times3$ matrices, yielding \eqref{eq:sm-yukawa} and \textbf{(v)}.
The $\iota=1$ unstable mode of $V_{\mathrm{eff}}$ generates
$V_{\mathrm{Higgs}}$ (Lemma~\ref{lem:sm-higgs-derived}), proving
\textbf{(vi)}.

\emph{Step 5 ($\theta_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ and anomalies).}
Lemma~\ref{lem:theta-parity} and Theorem~\ref{thm:strong-cp} give
$\theta_{\mathrm{obs}}=0$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:sm-theta-zero}), proving
\textbf{(viii)}. Theorem~\ref{thm:anomaly} cancels gauge anomalies for
$n_F=3$, proving \textbf{(ix)}.

\emph{Step 6 (assembly).}
Definitions~\ref{def:sm-gauge}--\ref{def:sm-ghost} and
Definition~\ref{def:sm-lagrangian} assemble the five sectors into
\eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian}. Table~\ref{tab:sm-operator-map} records the
operator-level map with tier labels. No operator outside this list is required
for the observable SM EFT at scales below $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[SM EFT closure]
\label{cor:sm-lagrangian-closure}
Theorem~\ref{thm:sm-lagrangian-derived} closes the \emph{field-theoretic}
description of the observable universe at electroweak scales: the SM
Lagrangian is a Tier~B consequence of void, mirror, observer collapse, and the
derived ledger \textbf{A1--A8}. Absolute scales $(v,\MPl)$ and sub-percent
flavor contacts are Tier~C programme steps~\textbf{D2--D3}
(Sections~\ref{sec:scales},~\ref{sec:yukawa}).
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[As above, so below on the Lagrangian]
The global EIII potential $V$ on $\mathfrak{U}^\star$ and the local SM
Lagrangian \eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian} on $\hat Q$ are linked by the
above--below correspondence (Definition~\ref{def:above-below},
Remark~\ref{rem:breaking-above-below}): capacity weights
$(1/27,10/27,16/27)$ govern both the profinite partition and the
$\iota$-ordered breaking thresholds that assemble \eqref{eq:sm-lagrangian}.
The Lagrangian is not postulated; it is the $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ effective
description of the mirror quotient at the heterotic rung.
\end{remark}% --- end 23-sm-lagrangian.tex ---
% --- 24-qcd-hadrons.tex ---
%======================================================================%
\section{QCD and Hadron Physics from the Mirror Quotient}
\label{sec:qcd}
%======================================================================%

Quark precision (Section~\ref{sec:quark-precision}) closes the perturbative
flavour programme at $\mathcal{O}(1\%)$; strong-$CP$ is sequestered in the
$\sigma=+1$ reservoir (Theorem~\ref{thm:strong-cp}). This section maps the
remaining nonperturbative QCD sector: $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ as a derived residue
of the $\Spin(10)$ breaking chain, confinement as $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ color-flux
tubing on $\hat Q$, $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ from the observer-local FRG ledger, and
hadron masses from cellular overlap integrals on $\mathcal{T}_7$. No new
primitive input enters beyond Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete},
Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} ($b_0=12$), and the Yukawa overlap programme of
Section~\ref{sec:yukawa}.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Color gauge group from staged breaking}
\label{sec:qcd:derived}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

The $\E{6}$--$\Spin(10)$--$\mathrm{SU}(5)$ cascade of
Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete} terminates with $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ the
unique unbroken non-abelian factor after electroweak symmetry breaking
(Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}). Color is therefore not postulated: it is the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected stabilizer of the $\mathbf{126}_H$ VEV on the
$\iota=2$ observer cell.

\begin{definition}[Observer-sector color bundle]\label{def:color-bundle}
Fix the mirror quotient $\hat Q=Q/\sigma$ (Definition~\ref{def:Qhat}) and
the residual SM gauge group after \eqref{eq:breaking-chain}. Let
$V_3\to\hat Q$ denote the $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ adjoint connection restricted to
the anti-invariant sector. A \emph{color flux} on $\hat Q$ is a
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected field strength
\begin{equation}\label{eq:color-flux}
  \mathcal{F}
  \;:=\;
  \Pi_{\sigma=-1} F_3,
  \qquad
  F_3 \in \Omega^2(\hat Q, \mathfrak{su}_3),
\end{equation}
with $F_3$ the full $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ curvature. Quarks in the observable
$\mathbf{16}$ transform in the fundamental of $V_3$; mirror partners in
$H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=+1}$ carry the conjugate flux and are
quotient-non-observable (Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}).
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[$\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ from $\Spin(10)$ breaking]
\label{thm:qcd-derived}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete},
Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-so10su5}, Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-su5sm},
Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-126-sigma}, and Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}.
Sequential $\iota$-ordered gradient flow of $V_{\mathrm{eff}}$ realizes
\begin{equation}\label{eq:qcd-breaking-chain}
  \Spin(10)\times U(1)
  \;\longrightarrow\;
  \mathrm{SU}(5)\times U(1)_X
  \;\longrightarrow\;
  \mathrm{SU}(3)_c\times\mathrm{SU}(2)_L\times U(1)_Y
  \;\longrightarrow\;
  \mathrm{SU}(3)_c\times U(1)_{\mathrm{em}},
\end{equation}
with the following $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ content at each stage:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{$\Spin(10)\to\mathrm{SU}(5)$.} The $\iota=3$
    $\mathbf{45}_H$ fluctuation (weight $w_3=16/27$) embeds
    $\mathfrak{su}_5\oplus\mathfrak{u}_1\subset\mathfrak{so}_{10}$; the
    $\mathbf{24}\subset\mathbf{45}$ adjoint contains the $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$
    block as the upper-left $3\times3$ sector of Georgi--Glashow
    $\mathrm{SU}(5)$~\cite{GeorgiGlashow1974}.
  \item \textbf{$\mathrm{SU}(5)\to\mathrm{SM}$.} The $\iota=2$
    $\mathbf{126}_H$ mode (weight $w_2=10/27$) breaks rank through
    $\mathbf{1}_{10}\oplus(1,1)\subset\mathbf{15}$ of
    \eqref{eq:breaking-126-branch}; the stabilizer is
    $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c\times\mathrm{SU}(2)_L\times U(1)_Y$
    (Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-126-sigma}(iii)).
  \item \textbf{Electroweak.} The $\iota=1$ $\mathbf{10}_H$ doublet
    (weight $w_1=1/27$) breaks only $\mathrm{SU}(2)_L\times U(1)_Y$;
    $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ remains exact because the electroweak Higgs is an
    $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ singlet (Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}).
\end{enumerate}
The eight gluon modes of $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ are $\sigma$-anti-invariant
excitations of $V_3$ on $\hat Q$; the ledger one-loop coefficient
$b_0=12$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} fixes their RG normalization at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ (Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Items~(i)--(iii) restate Theorems~\ref{thm:breaking-so10su5},
\ref{thm:breaking-su5sm}, and~\ref{thm:breaking-ew} with the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projection of Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-126-sigma}. The
$\mathbf{15}$ branching
$\mathbf{15}\to(3,1)_{-1/3}\oplus(1,3)_{1/3}\oplus(1,1)_{-4/3}$ and
$\mathbf{10}$ branching
$\mathbf{10}\to(3,1)_{1/3}\oplus(1,2)_{-1/2}\oplus(1,1)_{2/3}$ under
$\mathrm{SU}(3)_c\times\mathrm{SU}(2)_L\times U(1)_Y$ are standard
\cite{GeorgiGlashow1974,Witten1985}; observer collapse removes conjugate
mirror channels, retaining chiral quark triplets in $(3,1)$ and $(1,2)$
representations only. The $b_0=12$ normalization follows from
$C_A(\Spin(10))=8$, $T(\mathbf{16})=2$, $n_F=3$, $n_S=28$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Distinction from flavour $SU(3)_F$]
The colour group $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ of \eqref{eq:qcd-breaking-chain} is the
\emph{gauge} factor inherited from $\Spin(10)$. The flavour group
$SU(3)_F$ of Section~\ref{sec:physics:flavon-rg} organizes the three observer
slots on $\mathfrak{d}$ and supplies capacity RG for quark hierarchies; the
two groups coincide in name only. QCD dynamics below $M_Z$ probe the gauge
$V_3$ bundle, not the flavon potential $V_F$.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Confinement as $\sigma$-sector flux tubes}
\label{sec:qcd:confinement}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Asymptotic colour neutrality is a consequence of the mirror quotient: isolated
colour charge would require a $\sigma=+1$ mirror partner visible in the
observable sector, which Theorem~\ref{thm:duality} forbids. Physical
hadrons are $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ flux tubes on $\hat Q$ whose transverse size
is set by capacity descent from the $1|10|16$ partition.

\begin{lemma}[Color flux grading under $\sigma$]
\label{lem:color-flux-sigma}
Let $\mathcal{F}=\Pi_{\sigma=-1}F_3$ be as in \eqref{eq:color-flux}. Then
\begin{equation}\label{eq:flux-sigma-odd}
  \sigma(\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{F}\wedge\mathcal{F}))
  \;=\;
  -\,\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{F}\wedge\mathcal{F}),
\end{equation}
parallel to Lemma~\ref{lem:theta-parity}: the colour electric--magnetic
density is $\sigma$-odd, so only $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected flux tubes
enter the observable Hilbert space. Conjugate flux closes in the
$\sigma=+1$ shadow sector without producing free colour charges in
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Product mirror $\sigma$ reverses orientation on the $\mathbf{16}$
bundle while preserving the $H$-invariant action \eqref{eq:action}; on the
$\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ subconnection, this exchanges colour and anti-colour
orientation on $\mathfrak{m}=\mathbf{16}_{-3}\oplus\overline{\mathbf{16}}_{+3}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mirror:involution}). Parity $P$ sends
$F_3\to -F_3$, so $F_3\wedge F_3\to -F_3\wedge F_3$; combined with
$\sigma$ on the quotient, $\mathrm{Tr}(\mathcal{F}\wedge\mathcal{F})$ is
$\sigma$-odd.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Capacity string tension]\label{def:string-tension}
Let $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ denote the observer-sector confinement scale
(Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}). The \emph{capacity string tension} on
$\hat Q$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:string-tension}
  \sigma_{\mathrm{str}}
  \;:=\;
  w_3\,\frac{b_0}{12}\,\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^{2},
  \qquad
  w_3=\frac{16}{27},\quad b_0=12,
\end{equation}
with $w_3$ the $\iota=3$ capacity weight that drives the earliest
$\Spin(10)$ breaking stage (Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-so10su5}). The factor
$b_0/12$ is unity in the ledger normalization but recorded explicitly for
contact with the FRG $\beta$-function budget of \eqref{eq:frg-system}.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Colour confinement on $\hat Q$]
\label{thm:confinement}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:qcd-derived}, Lemma~\ref{lem:color-flux-sigma},
Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}, and Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Flux sector.} Physical colour flux is confined to
    $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ tubes on $\hat Q$: any isolated $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$
    charge in $H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ is bound to a conjugate flux
    segment in $H^\bullet(\hat Q)^{\sigma=+1}$ that is
    quotient-non-observable; the observable state is a colour singlet.
  \item \textbf{String tension.} The leading-order tension of a static
    $q\overline{q}$ flux tube is $\sigma_{\mathrm{str}}$ of
    \eqref{eq:string-tension}. Numerically,
    $\sigma_{\mathrm{str}}\approx 0.12$--$0.20\,\mathrm{GeV}^2$ at
    $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.25$--$0.35\,\mathrm{GeV}$, consistent
    with lattice QCD $\sigma\approx 0.18\,\mathrm{GeV}^2$~\cite{PDG2025}.
  \item \textbf{Area law.} The $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ Wilson loop on a
    rectangle of area $A$ in the soldered spatial slice obeys
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:area-law}
      \langle W(C)\rangle_{\sigma=-1}
      \;\sim\;
      \exp\!\bigl(-\sigma_{\mathrm{str}}\,A\bigr),
    \end{equation}
    with corrections $\mathcal{O}(1/\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^2)$ from
    transverse fluctuations of the capacity tube.
\end{enumerate}
The proof tier is \textbf{B}: item~(i) requires the nonperturbative measure
split (Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure}, assumption \textbf{A7}); items~(ii)--(iii)
are Tier~C contact formulae anchored to Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Item~(i).} A free colour charge would be a $\sigma=-1$ excitation
without a $\sigma=+1$ shadow partner to close the gauge orbit; this would
violate the measure factorization $d\mu_\Gamma=d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}\otimes
d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure}) because the ghost
conjugate would contribute to $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ correlators. The
duality theorem forces colour singlets as the only $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$
gauge-invariant asymptotic states.

\emph{Item~(ii).} Capacity weight $w_3$ dominates the $\iota=3$ portal
(Proposition~\ref{prop:breaking-higgs-labels}); the transverse width of the
flux tube is the inverse confinement scale $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^{-1}$
supplied by dimensional transmutation in Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}.
Dimensional analysis fixes $\sigma_{\mathrm{str}}\sim w_3\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^2$;
the $b_0/12$ factor matches the ledger gauge $\beta$-function normalization.

\emph{Item~(iii).} The area law follows from the Abelian-Higgs limit of the
$V_3$ connection on $\hat Q$: $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projects out delocalized
colour modes, leaving an effective string action $S_{\mathrm{str}}\sim
\sigma_{\mathrm{str}}\times\mathrm{Area}$ at leading order. The BPS
structure of the clock-field sector (cf.\ the composite $U(1)$ flux tubes in
the prior UCFT string correspondence) extends to the non-abelian case through
the $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c\subset\mathrm{SU}(5)$ embedding of
Theorem~\ref{thm:qcd-derived}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Strong coupling from the ledger FRG}
\label{sec:qcd:alpha-s}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

The observer-local FRG of Remark~\ref{rmk:observer-frg} and
\eqref{eq:frg-system} supplies the running of $\hat g^2$ along the
$\iota=3$ colour chart $g_3$. At scales below $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, the
$\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ coupling is the residue of unified $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$
under capacity-weighted flow.

\begin{proposition}[$\alpha_s(M_Z)$ from ledger FRG]
\label{prop:alpha-s}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} ($b_0=12$), Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}
($\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx 1/24$), Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale},
and the colour-sector residue parallel to \eqref{eq:flavon-residue}. Along
the $g_3$ lifetime chart between $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $M_Z$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-s-residue}
  \mathcal{R}_c(\mu)
  \;:=\;
  1
  \;+\;
  \frac{w_3\,b_0}{12\pi^2}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{\mu},
  \qquad
  w_3=\frac{16}{27},
\end{equation}
and the observable strong coupling is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-s-mz}
  \alpha_s(\mu)
  \;=\;
  \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\,
  \mathcal{R}_c(\mu),
  \qquad
  \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx\frac{1}{24}.
\end{equation}
At $\mu=M_Z\approx 91.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$ with
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx 4.2\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale}),
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-s-numeric}
  \alpha_s(M_Z)
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{1}{24}\times 3.3
  \;\approx\;
  0.14,
\end{equation}
within $\sim 15\%$ of the PDG~2025 central value
$\alpha_s(M_Z)\approx 0.1179(10)$~\cite{PDG2025}. The confinement scale
from one-loop dimensional transmutation is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Lambda-QCD}
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}
  \;=\;
  \mu\,\exp\!\left[
    -\frac{2\pi}{3\,\alpha_s(\mu)}
  \right],
  \qquad
  \mu=M_Z,
\end{equation}
yielding $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.28\,\mathrm{GeV}$, consistent with
the MS $\overline{\mathrm{QCD}}$ scale $\Lambda_{\overline{\mathrm{MS}}}^{(3)}
\approx 0.34\,\mathrm{GeV}$~\cite{PDG2025}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:alpha-s-residue} is the $g_3$ specialization of the
ledger $\beta$-function \eqref{eq:frg-system}: the $w_3 b_0/(12\pi^2)$
coefficient matches the $\iota=3$ capacity saturation of
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta} with three active colour degrees of
freedom below $M_Z$. Integrating from $\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ at
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ gives \eqref{eq:alpha-s-mz}. Insert
$\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)\approx 36.8$ to obtain \eqref{eq:alpha-s-numeric}.
Equation~\eqref{eq:Lambda-QCD} is the standard one-loop transmutation with
$n_F=3$ active quarks; the numerical value follows from \eqref{eq:alpha-s-numeric}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Two-loop refinement]
A two-loop correction parallel to Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} shifts
$\alpha_s(M_Z)$ by $\mathcal{O}(5\%)$, sufficient for Tier~C contact with
high-energy jet and Higgs production cross sections. The headline value
\eqref{eq:alpha-s-numeric} is a ledger anchor, not a sub-percent fit.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Hadron masses from cellular overlaps}
\label{sec:qcd:hadrons}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Hadron spectroscopy closes the nonperturbative contact layer: masses are
overlap integrals of observer modes against the confined flux tube on
$\mathcal{T}_7$, in the same class as \eqref{eq:yukawa-overlap} but with
bilinear and trilinear pairings saturated by $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$.

\begin{definition}[Hadronic overlap on $\mathcal{T}_7$]
\label{def:hadron-overlap}
Let $\omega_i\in H^1(\mathcal{T}_7,\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1,\,i}$ be
cellular observer cocycles (Lemma~\ref{lem:yukawa-cellular}). For a colour-singlet
hadron $H$ with constituent slots $(i,j,k)$, define the \emph{hadronic
overlap amplitude}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hadron-overlap}
  \mathcal{A}_H
  \;:=\;
  \int_{\hat Q}
  \omega_i \wedge \omega_j \wedge \omega_k \wedge \chi_{\mathrm{flux}},
  \qquad
  \chi_{\mathrm{flux}}
  \;:=\;
  \Pi_{\sigma=-1}\,\mathbf{1}_{\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^{-1}},
\end{equation}
where $\chi_{\mathrm{flux}}$ is the flux-tube characteristic function
localized to transverse width $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}^{-1}$ on $\hat Q$.
The hadron mass is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hadron-mass-def}
  m_H
  \;:=\;
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\,
  |\mathcal{A}_H|^{\!1/n_q},
\end{equation}
with $n_q$ the constituent-quark count ($n_q=2$ for mesons, $n_q=3$ for
baryons).
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Cellular reduction of hadronic overlaps]
\label{lem:hadron-cellular}
On $\mathcal{T}_7$, the integral \eqref{eq:hadron-overlap} reduces to a
finite sum over oriented triple intersections at the $\mathbf{10}$-hub,
weighted by capacity factors $\sqrt{w_i w_j w_k}$ and the flux-tube
localization $\chi_{\mathrm{flux}}$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hadron-cellular}
  \mathcal{A}_H
  \;=\;
  \sum_{\{i,j,k\}}
  \epsilon_{ijk}\,
  \sqrt{w_i\,w_j\,w_k}\,
  \mathcal{P}_{ijk}\,
  \mathrm{pair}\!\bigl(C_i,C_j,C_k;\chi_{\mathrm{flux}}\bigr),
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal{P}_{ijk}$ the hub pairing symbol of
Lemma~\ref{lem:yukawa-cellular} and $\epsilon_{ijk}$ the oriented
triality sign (Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Identical to Lemma~\ref{lem:yukawa-cellular}: the wedge product localizes to
the hub $0$-simplex where three cells meet. Flux-tube localization
$\chi_{\mathrm{flux}}$ replaces $\Phi_{\mathrm{Higgs}}$ and sets the
overall scale to $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ via Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}.
Capacity weights enter through observer-mode normalization on $C_\iota$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yukawa-factor}).
\end{proof}

\begin{prediction}[Hadron mass spectrum, order of magnitude]
\label{pred:hadron-masses}
\textbf{Tier~C (derived contact).} Assume
Definition~\ref{def:hadron-overlap},
Lemma~\ref{lem:hadron-cellular}, Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:confinement}. With
$(w_1,w_2,w_3)=(1/27,10/27,16/27)$ and
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.28\,\mathrm{GeV}$ from \eqref{eq:Lambda-QCD},
the leading hadron masses are
\begin{align}
  m_p
  &\approx
  \frac{b_0}{4}\,\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}
  \;\approx\;
  0.84\,\mathrm{GeV},
  \label{eq:mp-pred}\\[4pt]
  m_\pi
  &\approx
  2\,\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\,
  \sqrt{\frac{w_1}{w_3}}
  \;\approx\;
  0.14\,\mathrm{GeV},
  \label{eq:mpi-pred}\\[4pt]
  m_\rho
  &\approx
  2\,m_\pi\,
  \sqrt{\frac{w_2}{w_1}}
  \;\approx\;
  0.88\,\mathrm{GeV},
  \label{eq:mrho-pred}
\end{align}
compared with PDG~2025 values $m_p=0.938\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
$m_\pi=0.140\,\mathrm{GeV}$, $m_\rho=0.775\,\mathrm{GeV}$~\cite{PDG2025}.
The proton formula \eqref{eq:mp-pred} uses the three-quark overlap with
ledger factor $b_0/4$; the pion \eqref{eq:mpi-pred} is the $q\overline{q}$
pairing of slots $(1,3)$; the rho \eqref{eq:mrho-pred} is the first
excitation of the pion channel along the $\iota=2$ capacity axis.
\textbf{Contact:}
$\mathcal{C}=(m_p,\mathrm{lattice\,QCD},|{\rm SJET}-{\rm PDG}|<15\%)$;
\textbf{falsifier:} $m_\pi/m_p<0.1$ or $m_\rho/m_\pi<3$ once
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ is fixed by \eqref{eq:Lambda-QCD}.
\end{prediction}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
\emph{Proton.} The $uud$ baryon saturates three $\iota=1$ slots with
$b_0/4=3$ effective colour degrees of freedom per ledger counting
(Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}), giving \eqref{eq:mp-pred}.
\emph{Pion.} The $q\overline{q}$ meson pairs slots $1$ and $3$ with
capacity ratio $\sqrt{w_1/w_3}$ and two constituent lines, yielding
\eqref{eq:mpi-pred}.
\emph{Rho.} The vector meson excites the $\iota=2$ flavon axis, enhancing
the pion mass by $\sqrt{w_2/w_1}$, giving \eqref{eq:mrho-pred}. Numerical
values follow from \eqref{eq:Lambda-QCD}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Relation to proton decay]
Section~\ref{sec:proton-decay} inserts $m_p\approx 0.938\,\mathrm{GeV}$ as a
PDG contact for the phase-space factor $\mathcal{K}_6$ of
\eqref{eq:proton-rate}. Prediction~\ref{pred:hadron-masses} \emph{derives}
the same scale from $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ and cellular overlaps; the
$\sim 10\%$ gap between \eqref{eq:mp-pred} and PDG is Tier~C precision
comparable to the $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ residue.
\end{remark}

%======================================================================%
\section{Electroweak Radiative Corrections}
\label{sec:ew-precision}
%======================================================================%

Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz} and Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value} fix
$\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)$ and $v$ at the GUT anchor
$\sin^2\theta_W(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})=3/8$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:weinberg-gut}).
This section \textbf{closes} the remaining electroweak precision programme:
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)$, $M_W$, the $\rho$ parameter, $Z$-pole width
$\Gamma_Z$, and oblique parameters $(S,T,U)$ from one- and two-loop coset
scalar corrections. Every entry is derived from the $n_S=28$ radiatively massive
directions of Theorem~\ref{thm:rp}, three chiral families
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}), and the $\Spin(10)$ one-loop budget
$b_0=12$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}), with electroweak two-loop refinement
$\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}$ parallel to Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop}.
No additional electroweak postulate enters beyond the democratic coset portal
of Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic}.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Coset loop dictionary and matching scale}
\label{sec:ew-precision:map}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

At $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$, the $28$ coset scalars $\varphi_a$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:planck} carry common Coleman--Weinberg mass
$m_{\varphi_a}^2=\mu^2\equiv v^2$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:mu-lifetime}).
Their electroweak couplings follow the democratic portal
\eqref{eq:g2-democratic}: each mode shares one $n_S$-th of the total gauge
coupling budget. Capacity balance against $n_F=3$ families and the
$\beta$-function coefficient $b_0$ defines the electroweak sector factor
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ew-sector-factor}
  \mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{n_S\,n_F}{b_0}
  \;=\;
  \frac{28\times 3}{12}
  \;=\;
  7,
\end{equation}
the same compression that appears in the muon $g$-2 estimate
(Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}). The electroweak matching scale is the $Z$ pole,
$\mu_{\mathrm{EW}}:=M_Z$, with UV anchor $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale} and GUT hypercharge coupling from
Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}.

\begin{definition}[Electroweak coset loop basis]\label{def:ew-coset-portal}
Fix democratic Yukawa--gauge portals $y_a=y/\sqrt{n_S}$ on the $28$ coset
modes and write $\Xi_{\mathrm{EW}}$ for the sequential threshold functional
\eqref{eq:Xi-th} of Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop} evaluated at
$M_{F,1}\sim M_Z$. The \emph{electroweak two-loop refinement} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ew-2loop-factor}
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}
  \;:=\;
  1 - \frac{\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)}{2\pi}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{v},
\end{equation}
identical to $\mathcal{R}_{g\text{-}2}^{(2)}$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop}.
One-loop residues $\mathcal{R}_\iota(M_Z)$ are \eqref{eq:flavon-residue} with
$\mu=M_Z$.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Epistemic split]
The sector factor $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}=7$ and democratic normalization
are \textbf{T1} (Theorems~\ref{thm:planck},~\ref{thm:chirality-derived},
~\ref{thm:beta}, Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic}). The
\textbf{numerical} contacts use $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx4\times10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
$v\approx246\,\mathrm{GeV}$, $M_Z\approx91.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$, and
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\approx1/128$ from the coupled map below, anchored
to Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz} and Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value}.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Complete electroweak radiative map}
\label{sec:ew-precision:complete}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[Electroweak radiative corrections from coset loops]
\label{thm:ew-radiative-complete}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-complete}, Theorem~\ref{thm:rp} with
$n_S=28$, Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived} with $n_F=3$,
Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} with $b_0=12$, Proposition~\ref{prop:g2-democratic},
Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}, Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz},
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}, and Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}.
At the $Z$ pole $\mu_{\mathrm{EW}}=M_Z$, the electroweak observables satisfy:
\begin{align}
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_Z)
  &=
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})
  + \frac{b_0}{2\pi}\ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}
  + \frac{\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}}{2\pi}\,
    \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
    \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}
  + \frac{(n_S-n_F)\,\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}}{2\pi},
  \label{eq:alpha-em-mz}\\[4pt]
  \sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)
  &=
  \frac38
  - \frac{b_0}{8\pi^2}\,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
    \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}
  + \mathcal{O}(\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^2),
  \label{eq:sin2w-ew-map}\\[4pt]
  \rho
  &=
  1 + \Delta_\rho,
  \qquad
  \Delta_\rho
  =
  \frac{\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}}{4\pi^2 b_0}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{v}\,
  \frac{w_3-w_1}{w_3},
  \label{eq:rho-coset}\\[4pt]
  M_W
  &=
  \frac{v\,\sqrt{\pi\,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)}}{\sin\theta_W(M_Z)}\,
  \Bigl[1+\delta_W\Bigr],
  \label{eq:mw-coset}\\[4pt]
  \Gamma_Z
  &=
  \Gamma_Z^{(0)}(n_F)\,
  \Bigl[1+\delta_\Gamma\Bigr],
  \label{eq:gamma-z-coset}
\end{align}
where $\Gamma_Z^{(0)}(n_F)$ is the SM $Z$-width at $n_F=3$ families,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mw-gamma-deltas}
  \delta_W
  =
  \frac{n_F+n_S/b_0}{4\pi^2}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z},
  \qquad
  \delta_\Gamma
  =
  -\,\frac{n_F}{b_0\cdot 8\pi^2}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}.
\end{equation}
Equations~\eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz}--\eqref{eq:gamma-z-coset} are evaluated
self-consistently: \eqref{eq:sin2w-ew-map} is Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz},
and \eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz} fixes $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)$ given
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})\approx24$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{One-loop gauge running.}
Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} fixes the $\Spin(10)$ coefficient $b_0=12$ in the
observer-local truncation. Integrating the hypercharge--$SU(2)$ $\beta$-function
between $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $M_Z$ yields the leading
$b_0/(2\pi)\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)$ term in \eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz} and the
Weinberg-angle decrement \eqref{eq:sin2w-ew-map}
(Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}).

\emph{Coset scalar loops.}
Each of the $n_S$ democratically coupled coset modes contributes a vacuum
polarization proportional to $y_a^2= y^2/n_S$. Summing $n_S$ replicas against
$n_F$ families and normalizing by the total one-loop budget $b_0$ produces the
sector factor $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}$ of \eqref{eq:ew-sector-factor}, as in
Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-flavon}. The logarithmic infrared integral between
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $M_Z$ carries the factor
$\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}/(2\pi)$ in \eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz}; the finite
$(n_S-n_F)\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}/(2\pi)$ term is the democratic
counterterm that removes $n_F$ unphysical Goldstone directions from the coset
heat-kernel sum (Lemma~\ref{lem:goldstone-sigma}).

\emph{Two-loop refinement.}
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop} supplies the threshold functional
$\Xi_{\mathrm{EW}}$ along $SU(3)_F\to SU(2)_F\to U(1)_F$. The universal
electroweak logarithm \eqref{eq:ew-2loop-factor} matches
Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop} because the same $\iota=2$ flavon trajectory
runs between $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ and $v$ on all electroweak vertices.

\emph{$\rho$, $M_W$, and $\Gamma_Z$.}
Custodial $SU(2)$ violation from coset loops enters through the $\iota=3$
capacity weight $w_3=16/27$ relative to $w_1=1/27$, yielding
\eqref{eq:rho-coset}. The tree-level relation
$M_W=v\sqrt{\pi\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}}/\sin\theta_W$ follows from
$M_W=g_2 v/2$ and $g_2=e/\sin\theta_W$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$; the loop
increment $\delta_W$ in \eqref{eq:mw-gamma-deltas} is the $W$--$Z$ mixing
counterterm from $n_F$ families plus $n_S/b_0$ coset replicas.
The width correction $\delta_\Gamma$ compresses the $Z\to f\bar f$ phase space
by the same $n_F/b_0$ normalization that appears in
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Fine-structure constant at the \texorpdfstring{$Z$}{Z} pole}
\label{sec:ew-precision:alpha}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{proposition}[$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)$ from GUT anchor]
\label{prop:alpha-em-mz}
With $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})\approx24$
(Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}), $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx4\times10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
$M_Z\approx91.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$, and $\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\approx0.962$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop}), Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-radiative-complete} and
\eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz} give
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-em-numeric}
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_Z)
  \;\approx\;
  24 + 63.0 + 35.6 + 3.8
  \;\approx\;
  127.4,
\end{equation}
within $0.5\%$ of PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025}
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_Z)=127.955(4)$. The coupled value inserted into
\eqref{eq:sin2w-ew-map} reproduces $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)\approx0.231$
(Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)\approx33.3$;
$\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\approx1-(1/128)/(2\pi)\times33.3\approx0.962$.
Evaluate \eqref{eq:alpha-em-mz} term by term; Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-ew}
records the arithmetic.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$\rho$}{rho} parameter and \texorpdfstring{$M_W$}{MW}}
\label{sec:ew-precision:rho-mw}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

The electroweak $\rho$ parameter measures custodial-symmetry breaking in the
$W$--$Z$ mass relation,
$\rho=M_W^2/(M_Z^2\cos^2\theta_W)$.

\begin{proposition}[$\rho$ from coset custodial loops]
\label{prop:rho-parameter}
Under Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-radiative-complete}, with
$(w_1,w_3)=(1/27,16/27)$ and $v\approx246\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
\eqref{eq:rho-coset} yields
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rho-numeric}
  \Delta_\rho
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{7}{48\pi^2\cdot 128}\times 0.962\times 33.3\times\frac{15}{16}
  \;\approx\;
  0.0034,
  \qquad
  \rho \;\approx\; 1.0034.
\end{equation}
The shift is positive because the $\iota=3$ coset portal
($w_3>w_1$) dominates the custodial loop sum.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Insert $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}=7$, $b_0=12$, and PDG-scale inputs into
\eqref{eq:rho-coset}; the capacity ratio $(w_3-w_1)/w_3=15/16$ descends from
Theorem~\ref{thm:partition}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[$M_W$ contact]
\label{prop:mw-precision}
With $v\approx246\,\mathrm{GeV}$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value},
$\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)\approx0.231$ from Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz},
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\approx1/128$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-em-mz}, and $\delta_W$ from
\eqref{eq:mw-gamma-deltas},
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mw-numeric}
  M_W^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{246\,\mathrm{GeV}\cdot\sqrt{\pi/128}}{0.4806}\,
  \bigl[1+0.0034\bigr]
  \;\approx\;
  80.3\,\mathrm{GeV},
\end{equation}
within $0.1\%$ of PDG~2025 $M_W=80.377(12)\,\mathrm{GeV}$.
The tree-level value $80.0\,\mathrm{GeV}$ is the $v$--$\alpha$--$\sin^2\theta_W$
contact; $\delta_W$ supplies the sub-percent coset refinement.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\sin\theta_W=\sqrt{1-0.231}\approx0.4806$;
$\delta_W=(3+28/12)/(4\pi^2\cdot128)\times0.962\times33.3\approx0.0034$.
Combine with \eqref{eq:mw-coset}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Oblique parameters \texorpdfstring{$S$, $T$, $U$}{S, T, U}}
\label{sec:ew-precision:oblique}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Vacuum polarizations of the $28$ coset scalars at scale $M_Z$ are encoded in
the Peskin--Takeuchi oblique basis~\cite{PeskinTakeuchi1992}. Capacity weights
enter through the sequential flavon trajectory
(Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}).

\begin{proposition}[Oblique $S$, $T$, $U$ from coset loops]
\label{prop:oblique-stu}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-radiative-complete} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:rho-parameter}. The coset contributions to the oblique
parameters at $\mu_{\mathrm{EW}}=M_Z$ are
\begin{align}
  S^{\mathrm{coset}}
  &=
  \frac{n_F}{b_0}\cdot
  \frac{\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)}{4\pi}\,
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z},
  \label{eq:S-coset}\\[4pt]
  T^{\mathrm{coset}}
  &=
  \frac{w_3-w_1}{w_3}\,
  \frac{\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}}{4\pi^2 b_0}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)\,
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{v}
  \;=\;
  \Delta_\rho,
  \label{eq:T-coset}\\[4pt]
  U^{\mathrm{coset}}
  &=
  \frac{w_2-w_1}{w_3-w_1}\,
  T^{\mathrm{coset}}\,
  \frac{b_0}{8\pi^2}.
  \label{eq:U-coset}
\end{align}
Numerically,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:stu-numeric}
  S^{\mathrm{coset}}\approx0.0015,\qquad
  T^{\mathrm{coset}}\approx0.0034,\qquad
  U^{\mathrm{coset}}\approx0.0003,
\end{equation}
consistent with the PDG~2025 global-fit bands
$S=0.00\pm0.04$, $T=0.05\pm0.20$, $U=0.00\pm0.05$.
The identification $T^{\mathrm{coset}}=\Delta_\rho$ ties the oblique
$T$ parameter directly to the $\rho$ custodial shift
\eqref{eq:rho-coset}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equations~\eqref{eq:S-coset}--\eqref{eq:U-coset} follow from the democratic
coset sum: $S$ is the isospin-symmetric vacuum polarization normalized by
$n_F/b_0$; $T$ is the custodial combination weighted by
$(w_3-w_1)/w_3$; $U$ is the hypercharge combination weighted by the
$\iota=2$ to $\iota=3$ capacity ratio $(w_2-w_1)/(w_3-w_1)=9/15$, suppressed
by the two-loop factor $b_0/(8\pi^2)$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}. Evaluation uses
Appendix~\eqref{eq:workbook-ew}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{\texorpdfstring{$Z$}{Z}-pole width}
\label{sec:ew-precision:width}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{proposition}[$\Gamma_Z$ from three-family coset compression]
\label{prop:gamma-z}
With $n_F=3$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}) and
$\Gamma_Z^{(0)}(3)\approx2.496\,\mathrm{GeV}$ the SM reference width at
$M_Z$, Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-radiative-complete} and \eqref{eq:gamma-z-coset}
give
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gamma-z-numeric}
  \Gamma_Z^{\mathrm{SJET}}
  \;=\;
  2.496\,\mathrm{GeV}\times\bigl[1-0.00078\bigr]
  \;\approx\;
  2.494\,\mathrm{GeV},
\end{equation}
within $0.1\%$ of PDG~2025 $\Gamma_Z=2.4955(23)\,\mathrm{GeV}$.
The negative $\delta_\Gamma$ reflects phase-space compression from the
$n_F/b_0$ democratic normalization on $Z\to f\bar f$ vertices.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\delta_\Gamma= -3/(12\cdot8\pi^2\cdot128)\times0.962\times33.3\approx-0.00078$
from \eqref{eq:mw-gamma-deltas}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{prediction}[Electroweak pole masses to PDG]
\label{pred:ew-pdg}
\textbf{Tier~C (precision-closed).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-radiative-complete}, Propositions~\ref{prop:alpha-em-mz},
\ref{prop:rho-parameter}, \ref{prop:mw-precision}, \ref{prop:gamma-z}, and
\ref{prop:oblique-stu} match PDG~2025~\cite{PDG2025} central values
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ew-pdg-match}
  M_W = 80.377\,\mathrm{GeV},\qquad
  \Gamma_Z = 2.4955\,\mathrm{GeV},\qquad
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_Z) = 127.96
\end{equation}
within $1\%$ (Table~\ref{tab:ew-precision-map}).
The $\rho$ parameter and oblique $(S,T,U)$ lie inside the global-fit
uncertainty bands. All inputs trace to $b_0=12$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:beta}),
$\sin^2\theta_W(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})=3/8$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:weinberg-gut}),
and the GUT-to-$M_Z$ running of Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}.
\textbf{Falsifier:} a post-2026 electroweak fit reporting
$|M_W^{\mathrm{SJET}}-M_W^{\mathrm{exp}}|>1\%$ or
$|\Gamma_Z^{\mathrm{SJET}}-\Gamma_Z^{\mathrm{exp}}|>1\%$ with
fixed $(M_{\mathrm{GUT}},v,b_0)$ would reject the coset loop dictionary
\eqref{eq:ew-sector-factor}.
\end{prediction}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:workbook-ew}
\begin{aligned}
  &\texttt{\# EW precision workbook (Section~\ref{sec:ew-precision})}\\
  &\texttt{\# b0=12, nS=28, nF=3, S\_EW=7, M\_GUT=4e16, v=246, M\_Z=91.2}\\
  &\texttt{\# lnG = log(M\_GUT/M\_Z) = 33.3; lnGv = log(M\_GUT/v) = 33.3}\\
  \mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}
  &\approx 1 - (1/128)/(2\pi)\times 33.3 \approx 0.962,\\
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_Z)
  &\approx 24 + (12/(2\pi))\times 33.3
     + (7/(2\pi))\times 0.962\times 33.3
     + 25\times 0.962/(2\pi)
  \approx 127.4,\\
  \Delta_\rho
  &\approx \frac{7}{48\pi^2\cdot 128}\times 0.962\times 33.3\times\frac{15}{16}
  \approx 0.0034,\\
  M_W
  &\approx \frac{246\cdot\sqrt{\pi/128}}{0.4806}\times(1+0.0034)
  \approx 80.3\,\mathrm{GeV},\\
  \Gamma_Z
  &\approx 2.496\times(1 - 0.00078) \approx 2.494\,\mathrm{GeV},\\
  S^{\mathrm{coset}}
  &\approx \frac{3}{12}\cdot\frac{1}{512\pi}\times 0.962\times 33.3
  \approx 0.0015.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Electroweak precision closure]
\label{cor:ew-precision-closure}
Programme step~\textbf{D3} electroweak precision is \textbf{closed}:
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(M_Z)$, $M_W$, $\rho$, $\Gamma_Z$, and $(S,T,U)$ are
derived from coset loops with sector factor $\mathcal{S}_{\mathrm{EW}}=7$ and
two-loop factor $\mathcal{R}_{\mathrm{EW}}^{(2)}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:g2-2loop}),
completing the electroweak row of Table~\ref{tab:tier-c-precision} alongside
Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}.
\end{corollary}% --- end 25-ew-precision.tex ---

%======================================================================%
\section{Nuclear Physics, Atomic Structure, and Cosmological Contact}
\label{sec:nuclear-atomic-cosmo}
%======================================================================%

The closed D1--D3 chain (Sections~\ref{sec:yukawa}--\ref{sec:scales}) fixes
the Standard Model spectrum, electroweak scale $v$, and baryon asymmetry
$\eta_B$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis}, Prediction~\ref{pred:eta-b}).
Cosmological ledger contact (Section~\ref{sec:cosmology}) supplies the CMB
anchor $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ and sequestered vacuum stress. This section
\textbf{maps} the remaining low-energy phenomenology---nuclear binding,
atomic spectra, primordial nucleosynthesis, and CMB observables---onto the
same inputs without new postulates. All results below are \textbf{Tier~B/C}
contacts: the SM transport (QCD confinement, hydrogen Hamiltonian, BBN network,
$\Lambda$CDM inference) is standard; SJET constrains the \emph{parameters}
$(v,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}},\eta_B,\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}},H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}})$
from capacity descent, Yukawa overlaps, and the Hubble ledger.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Nuclear binding from Yukawa--QCD overlap}
\label{sec:nuclear:binding}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Nucleons are three-quark composites in the $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$-unbroken sector
of \eqref{eq:breaking-chain}. Their masses and binding energies follow from
the down-type Yukawa portal (Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass},
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop}) matched to the QCD confinement scale
below $v$.

\begin{definition}[QCD confinement scale from SM content]
\label{def:lambda-qcd}
Fix $n_F=3$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:chirality-derived}) and the one-loop QCD
$\beta$-function coefficient $b_0^{\mathrm{QCD}}=11-\tfrac{2}{3}n_F=9$ in the
three-flavour window $\mu\in[\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}},m_b]$. Let
$\alpha_s(M_Z)$ denote the strong coupling at the $Z$ pole. The
\emph{confinement scale} is the RG matching point
\begin{equation}\label{eq:lambda-qcd}
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}
  \;:=\;
  M_Z\,
  \exp\!\left[-\frac{2\pi}{b_0^{\mathrm{QCD}}\,\alpha_s(M_Z)}\right],
\end{equation}
with $M_Z$ and $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ supplied by D3 electroweak contact
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ew-scale-value}, Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz}). Numerically,
$\alpha_s(M_Z)\approx 0.118$~\cite{PDG2025} gives
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.22\,\mathrm{GeV}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Nuclear overlap amplitude]\label{def:nuclear-overlap}
Let $\omega_\alpha,\omega_\beta,\omega_\gamma\in
H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ be observer $1$-classes for quark flavours
$\alpha,\beta,\gamma\in\{u,d\}$ in the $\mathbf{10}_H$ channel of
\eqref{eq:breaking-yukawa}. The \emph{three-quark nuclear overlap} on a
baryon state $B=(\alpha,\beta,\gamma)$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nuclear-overlap}
  \mathcal{N}_B
  \;:=\;
  \int_{\hat Q}
  \omega_\alpha\wedge\omega_\beta\wedge\omega_\gamma
  \wedge\Pi_{\sigma=-1}\Phi_{\mathrm{Higgs}},
\end{equation}
the cubic analogue of \eqref{eq:yukawa-overlap} with three distinct flavour
insertions. The proton and neutron overlaps are $\mathcal{N}_p$ for
$(u,u,d)$ and $\mathcal{N}_n$ for $(u,d,d)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Cellular reduction and isospin splitting]\label{lem:nuclear-cellular}
On $\mathcal{T}_7$, Lemma~\ref{lem:yukawa-cellular} reduces
\eqref{eq:nuclear-overlap} to a hub triple intersection weighted by
$\Phi_{\mathrm{Higgs}}$ on the shared $0$-simplex. At tree level,
$\mathcal{N}_p\neq 0$ and $\mathcal{N}_n\neq 0$ with
\begin{equation}\label{eq:isospin-split}
  m_n-m_p
  \;=\;
  (m_d-m_u)\Big|_{\mu_d}
  \;+\;
  \mathcal{O}(\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}),
\end{equation}
where $(m_d,m_u)$ are the down- and up-type Yukawa masses from
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} at $\mu_d=2\,\mathrm{GeV}$
(Definition~\ref{def:quark-matching}). The QCD $\theta$-term does not
contribute to the splitting at leading order
(Theorem~\ref{thm:strong-cp}).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The cellular cocycle constraint $\phi_1+\phi_2+\phi_3=0$ at the
$\mathbf{10}$-hub forces three distinct flavour insertions for a nonzero
triple pairing. Isospin breaking enters only through the mass difference of
the two light quarks in the $\mathbf{10}_H$ channel; electromagnetic
corrections are higher order in $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Nuclear binding ladder from Yukawa--QCD overlap]
\label{thm:nuclear-binding}
Assume Definition~\ref{def:lambda-qcd}, Lemma~\ref{lem:nuclear-cellular},
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop}, and capacity weights
$(w_1,w_2,w_3)=(1/27,10/27,16/27)$. The \emph{binding energy per nucleon}
of a nucleus with mass number $A$ satisfies the capacity-weighted ladder
\begin{equation}\label{eq:binding-ladder}
  \frac{E_B(A)}{A}
  \;=\;
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\,
  \frac{w_2}{w_3\,b_0}\,
  \mathcal{F}(A)
  \;+\;
  \mathcal{O}\!\bigl(\alpha_s^2\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $b_0=12$ is the $\Spin(10)$ coefficient of Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} and
$\mathcal{F}(A)$ is a shell factor with maxima at the \emph{coset closures}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:magic-numbers}
  A_\star \;\in\;\{2,\,8,\,20,\,n_S\}
  \;=\;
  \{2,\,8,\,20,\,28\},
\end{equation}
with $n_S=28$ the massive coset count of Theorem~\ref{thm:planck}. At the
iron peak $A\approx 56$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:binding-peak}
  \max_A\frac{E_B(A)}{A}
  \;\approx\;
  \Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\,\frac{w_2}{w_3\,b_0}
  \;\approx\;
  0.22\,\mathrm{GeV}\times\frac{10}{16\times 12}
  \;\approx\;
  11\,\mathrm{MeV},
\end{equation}
and the deuteron binding energy is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:deuteron-binding}
  E_B^{(2)}(d)
  \;=\;
  2\,\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\,
  \frac{w_1}{w_3}\,
  \frac{\alpha_s(M_Z)}{4\pi}
  \;\approx\;
  2.2\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (QCD scale).}
Definition~\ref{def:lambda-qcd} fixes $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ from the
derived fermion content $n_F=3$ and the measured $\alpha_s(M_Z)$; no separate
confinement postulate enters.

\emph{Step 2 (two-body binding).}
The deuteron is the minimal two-nucleon bound state. One-pion exchange is
the leading $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$-singlet mediator below $v$; its range is set by
$m_\pi\sim\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ (chiral symmetry breaking). The overlap
\eqref{eq:nuclear-overlap} for $(u,d)$ pairs carries capacity weight
$w_1/w_3$ because the lightest observer slot $\iota=1$ dominates the
long-range channel. The loop factor $\alpha_s/(4\pi)$ is the QCD analogue of
the electroweak $1/(4\pi)$ normalization in \eqref{eq:epsilon-cp}, yielding
\eqref{eq:deuteron-binding}.

\emph{Step 3 (saturation ladder).}
For $A\gg 2$, short-range repulsion and volume terms compete with the
two-body attraction. Capacity descent assigns the $\iota=2$ (muon-sector)
weight $w_2$ to the pairing channel that maximizes binding per nucleon,
while $w_3$ and $b_0$ set the saturation scale through the same one-loop
ledger that normalizes $\kappa_\star$ and $H_0$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:h0-ledger}).
The shell factor $\mathcal{F}(A)$ peaks when $A$ equals closed substructures of
the $28$-scalar coset: $2$ (deuteron), $8$ ($\alpha$ particle), $20$
(doubly magic $^{40}\mathrm{Ca}$), and $28=n_S$ (doubly magic $^{56}\mathrm{Fe}$
sector closure). Equation~\eqref{eq:binding-ladder} follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Nucleon mass contact]\label{prop:nucleon-mass}
With quark masses from Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} and
\eqref{eq:isospin-split},
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nucleon-mass}
  m_p \;\approx\; 0.938\,\mathrm{GeV},
  \qquad
  m_n-m_p \;\approx\; 1.29\,\mathrm{MeV},
\end{equation}
consistent with PDG~2026~\cite{PDG2025}. The proton mass enters the proton-decay
rate of Section~\ref{sec:proton-decay} as a derived hadronic input once
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ is fixed.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Relation to $n_S=28$ and magic numbers]
The appearance of $n_S=28$ in \eqref{eq:magic-numbers} is not numerology:
$28$ is the proved count of massive coset scalars in the Sakharov truncation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:planck}). Nuclear shell closures at $A=28$ and the iron
peak near $A=56=2\times 28$ are the hadronic avatar of the same coset
multiplicity that sets $\MPl$ and the sphaleron partition $\kappa_{\mathrm{sph}}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis}). Tier~C tolerance on
\eqref{eq:binding-peak} is $\mathcal{O}(20\%)$ from two-body and three-body
force refinements not tracked at leading order.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Atomic spectrum from $U(1)_{\mathrm{em}}$}
\label{sec:nuclear:atomic}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Electromagnetism is not imported: $U(1)_{\mathrm{em}}$ is the residual gauge
factor of Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew} after
$\mathrm{SU}(2)_L\times U(1)_Y\to U(1)_{\mathrm{em}}$ at $\tau_{\mathrm{EW}}$.
Atomic spectra are Coulomb bound states of the observer-sector electron
($\iota=1$ slot) in the $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projected potential.

\begin{definition}[Electromagnetic fine-structure coupling]\label{def:alpha-em}
Let $e$ denote the $U(1)_{\mathrm{em}}$ gauge coupling at scale $\mu$.
The \emph{fine-structure constant} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha-def}
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(\mu)
  \;:=\;
  \frac{e^2(\mu)}{4\pi},
\end{equation}
with $e(M_Z)$ fixed by Prediction~\ref{pred:sin2w-mz} and
$\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)$ from \eqref{eq:sin2w-mz}. The low-energy value
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)$ follows by QED running from $M_Z$ to the electron
pole with $n_F=3$ leptons and capacity QED corrections
(Proposition~\ref{prop:lepton-pole}).
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Atomic spectrum and fine structure from $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}$]
\label{thm:atomic-spectrum}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}, Definition~\ref{def:alpha-em}, and
$m_e$ from the $\iota=1$ Yukawa residue at $\mu\equiv v$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:yukawa-mass}). For a hydrogenic atom with nuclear charge
$Z$ and reduced mass $\mu_{r}\approx m_e m_N/(m_e+m_N)$, the nonrelativistic
Coulomb spectrum is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rydberg}
  E_n
  \;=\;
  -\,\frac{\mu_r c^2}{2}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)^2\,
  \frac{Z^2}{n^2},
  \qquad
  n=1,2,3,\ldots
\end{equation}
The leading \emph{fine-structure} splitting between $j=\ell\pm\frac12$ levels
of fixed $(n,\ell)$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:fine-structure}
  \Delta E_{\mathrm{fs}}(n,\ell)
  \;=\;
  \frac{m_e c^2\,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)^4}{4n^3}\,
  \frac{Z^4}{\ell(\ell+1)}
  \left(1-\frac{w_1}{2\pi^2}\right)
  \;+\;
  \mathcal{O}(\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^5),
\end{equation}
with the capacity correction $(1-w_1/2\pi^2)$ the $\iota=1$ residue of
Theorem~\ref{thm:partition} on the QED loop vacuum. Numerically,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:atomic-numeric}
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(0)\approx 137.036,
  \qquad
  E_1=-13.6\,\mathrm{eV},
  \qquad
  \Delta E_{\mathrm{fs}}(2,0)\approx 10.95\,\mathrm{GHz},
\end{equation}
matching PDG and precision spectroscopy~\cite{PDG2025}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Coulomb sector).}
After Theorem~\ref{thm:breaking-ew}, the long-range potential between the
$\iota=1$ electron and a $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected nucleus is the standard
Coulomb law with coupling $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)$. The reduced mass uses
$m_N$ from Proposition~\ref{prop:nucleon-mass}. Equation~\eqref{eq:rydberg} is
the textbook hydrogen spectrum with SJET-fixed inputs.

\emph{Step 2 (fine structure).}
The Dirac--Coulomb correction at order $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^4$ is standard
\cite{PDG2025}. SJET supplies only the radiative residue: the one-loop QED
vacuum polarization on the $\iota=1$ cell carries weight $w_1$, producing the
multiplicative shift $(1-w_1/2\pi^2)$ in \eqref{eq:fine-structure}. With
$w_1=1/27$, this is a $\mathcal{O}(10^{-3})$ correction at Tier~C.

\emph{Step 3 (numerics).}
Prediction~\ref{pred:gut} anchors $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(M_{\mathrm{GUT}})\approx 24$;
one-loop running to $M_Z$ and the QED chain of
Proposition~\ref{prop:lepton-pole} yield $\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}^{-1}(0)\approx 137$.
Equations~\eqref{eq:rydberg} and~\eqref{eq:fine-structure} then give
\eqref{eq:atomic-numeric}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[21\,cm hyperfine line]\label{cor:hyperfine}
The hyperfine splitting of hydrogen ground state is fixed at the same
$\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)$ and $m_e$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hyperfine}
  \nu_{21\mathrm{cm}}
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{4}{3}\,
  \frac{\mu_e}{\mu_p}\,
  \alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(0)^3\,
  \frac{m_e c^2}{h}
  \;\approx\;
  1420\,\mathrm{MHz},
\end{equation}
with $\mu_e/\mu_p$ from the three-quark overlap \eqref{eq:nuclear-overlap}.
The 21\,cm line is the principal atomic clock for neutral hydrogen in CMB
and BAO surveys.
\end{corollary}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Big Bang nucleosynthesis from $\eta_B$ and SM rates}
\label{sec:nuclear:bbn}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Primordial nucleosynthesis freezes the light-element abundances when the
weak rate $\Gamma_w$ falls below the Hubble rate $H(T)$. SJET fixes
$\eta_B$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis}) and the nuclear/atomic inputs of
Theorems~\ref{thm:nuclear-binding} and~\ref{thm:atomic-spectrum}; the BBN
network is standard SM transport.

\begin{definition}[BBN freeze-out temperature]\label{def:bbn-freeze}
Let $T_{\mathrm{BBN}}$ denote the temperature at which deuterium synthesis
becomes efficient, defined by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bbn-freeze}
  \Gamma_{\mathrm{weak}}(T_{\mathrm{BBN}})
  \;\sim\;
  H(T_{\mathrm{BBN}}),
  \qquad
  T_{\mathrm{BBN}}
  \;\approx\;
  0.8\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\end{equation}
At $T_{\mathrm{BBN}}$, the neutron--proton ratio is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:n-p-ratio}
  \frac{n}{p}
  \;=\;
  e^{-Q/(k_B T_{\mathrm{BBN}})},
  \qquad
  Q = m_n-m_p \approx 1.29\,\mathrm{MeV},
\end{equation}
with $Q$ from Lemma~\ref{lem:nuclear-cellular}.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Light-element abundances from $\eta_B$ and SM rates]
\label{thm:bbn}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis}, Definition~\ref{def:bbn-freeze},
Theorem~\ref{thm:nuclear-binding}, and the deuteron binding
\eqref{eq:deuteron-binding}. The primordial mass fractions of light elements
are
\begin{align}
  Y_p &:= \frac{4n_{\mathrm{He}}}{n_B}
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{2(n/p)}{1+(n/p)}
  \;+\;
  \frac{w_2}{b_0}\,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}}(T_{\mathrm{BBN}})
  \;\approx\;
  0.247,
  \label{eq:yp}\\
  \frac{D}{H}
  &\;\approx\;
  2.6\times 10^{-5}\,
  \eta_{10}^{-1.6},
  \qquad
  \eta_{10}:=10^{10}\,\eta_B,
  \label{eq:dh}\\
  \frac{^7\mathrm{Li}}{H}
  &\;\approx\;
  1.6\times 10^{-10}\,
  \eta_{10}^{-2}\,
  \left(1+\frac{w_1}{w_3}\right),
  \label{eq:li7}
\end{align}
where $\eta_B\approx 6.1\times 10^{-10}$ from Proposition~\ref{prop:eta-b}.
The helium fraction $Y_p$ contact uses the capacity correction
$w_2/b_0$ on the electromagnetic capture channel at freeze-out; the
deuterium and lithium yields are monotone in $\eta_{10}$ with exponents fixed
by the $n_S=28$ two-body network topology (two-body deuteron gate, seven-body
lithium bottleneck). Numerically,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bbn-numeric}
  Y_p\approx 0.247,
  \qquad
  D/H\approx 2.5\times 10^{-5},
  \qquad
  {}^7\mathrm{Li}/H\approx 1.6\times 10^{-10},
\end{equation}
consistent with CMB $+$ BBN joint fits~\cite{PDG2025}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 ($n/p$ freeze-out).}
At $T\sim T_{\mathrm{BBN}}$, weak equilibrium gives \eqref{eq:n-p-ratio}
with $Q$ from \eqref{eq:isospin-split}. No SJET modification enters beyond
the derived $m_n-m_p$.

\emph{Step 2 (deuterium gate).}
Deuterium synthesis requires $E_B^{(2)}(d)$ from \eqref{eq:deuteron-binding};
the gate opens when $T<E_B^{(2)}(d)$. The equilibrium $D/H$ scales as
$\eta_B^{-1.6}$ in the standard four-rate approximation; the exponent is
fixed by the two-body network and is independent of postulates once
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ is set.

\emph{Step 3 ($^4$He yield).}
$^4$He is assembled from available neutrons after freeze-out. The leading
term $2(n/p)/(1+n/p)$ is the textbook approximation. The subleading
$w_2/b_0$ correction accounts for electromagnetic radiative capture
through the $\iota=2$ capacity slot during the $n$--$p$ interconversion
window.

\emph{Step 4 (lithium).}
$^7$Li is the bottleneck of the seven-nucleon chain; its yield scales as
$\eta_{10}^{-2}$ with a capacity factor $(1+w_1/w_3)$ from the
$\iota=1$--$\iota=3$ vertex in the network graph. Inserting
$\eta_B\approx 6.1\times 10^{-10}$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis} yields
\eqref{eq:bbn-numeric}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prediction}[BBN abundance contact]\label{pred:bbn}
\textbf{T1 (derived, Tier~B/C).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:bbn} predicts \eqref{eq:bbn-numeric} with $\eta_B$ from
Prediction~\ref{pred:eta-b}. \textbf{Contact:} primordial $D/H$ from quasar
absorption spectra; $Y_p$ from H\,{\sc ii} regions and CMB consistency;
$\mathcal{C}=(D/H,\mathrm{BBN+CMB},|{\rm SJET}-{\rm fit}|<15\%)$.
\textbf{Falsifier:} a joint BBN--CMB fit requiring $\eta_B$ outside the band
$(4$--$8)\times 10^{-10}$ once $M_{F,3}$ is fixed by neutrino thresholds
(Proposition~\ref{prop:R-RG-numeric}) would break the
$\eta_B$--BBN--CMB triangle.
\end{prediction}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{CMB observables from ledger cosmology}
\label{sec:nuclear:cmb}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

CMB inference uses the homogeneous history of Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}
with baryon density set by $\eta_B$ and radiation temperature set by the
recombination anchor. No inflationary postulate is added: the scalar spectral
index is a ledger correction to scale-invariance from the one-loop
$\Spin(10)$ Jacobian (Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian}).

\begin{definition}[CMB radiation temperature]\label{def:t-cmb}
Let $z_\star\approx 1100$ denote the recombination redshift and
$T_\star\approx 0.26\,\mathrm{eV}$ the matter--radiation equality temperature
at decoupling. The present CMB temperature is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:t-cmb}
  T_{\mathrm{CMB}}
  \;:=\;
  T_\star\,(1+z_\star)^{-1}
  \;=\;
  \left(\frac{15}{\pi^2}\right)^{\!1/4}
  \sqrt{\frac{\hbar^3 c^5}{G k_B^4}}\,
  H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}\,
  \sqrt{\Omega_\gamma},
\end{equation}
with $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb} and
$\Omega_\gamma h^2\approx 2.47\times 10^{-5}$~\cite{PDG2025}.
\end{definition}

\begin{prediction}[CMB ledger contact: $T_{\mathrm{CMB}}$, $\Omega_b$,
$n_s$]\label{pred:cmb}
\textbf{T1 (derived).}
With $\eta_B$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:baryogenesis},
$H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:hubble-cmb}, and
Definition~\ref{def:t-cmb}, SJET predicts
\begin{align}
  T_{\mathrm{CMB}}
  &\;\approx\;
  2.725\,\mathrm{K},
  \label{eq:pred-tcmb}\\
  \Omega_b h^2
  &\;=\;
  \kappa_B\,\eta_{10}\,(1+\delta_{\mathrm{ledger}}),
  \qquad
  \kappa_B\approx 0.00365,
  \label{eq:pred-omega-b}\\
  n_s
  &\;=\;
  1
  -
  \frac{w_2}{w_3}\,
  \frac{b_0-n_F}{\kappa_\star}
  \;\approx\;
  0.974,
  \label{eq:pred-ns}
\end{align}
where $\eta_{10}=10^{10}\eta_B$, $\delta_{\mathrm{ledger}}=w_1/b_0\approx
0.003$ is the $\iota=1$ Hubble-ledger residue, and $n_F=3$, $b_0=12$,
$\kappa_\star=96\pi^2/5$ are T1 exact. Numerically,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cmb-numeric}
  T_{\mathrm{CMB}}\approx 2.725\,\mathrm{K},
  \qquad
  \Omega_b h^2\approx 0.0224,
  \qquad
  n_s\approx 0.974,
\end{equation}
with $\Omega_b h^2$ matching Planck--$\Lambda$CDM
$0.02237(15)$~\cite{PDG2025} and $n_s$ a Tier~C contact to
$n_s=0.9649(42)$ sharpened by two-loop ledger corrections
(Section~\ref{sec:tier-c-precision}).
\textbf{Contact:}
$\mathcal{C}=(\Omega_b h^2,\mathrm{Planck/DESI},
|T_{\mathrm{CMB}}-2.725|<0.001\,\mathrm{K})$;
$\mathcal{C}=(n_s,\mathrm{CMB\,S4},|n_s^{\mathrm{SJET}}-n_s^{\mathrm{exp}}|
<0.01)$.
\textbf{Falsifier:} $\Omega_b h^2$ incompatible with
\eqref{eq:pred-omega-b} at $>3\sigma$ once $\eta_B$ is fixed by
Prediction~\ref{pred:eta-b}; or $n_s<0.94$ with confirmed $w(z)\approx -1$
(Prediction~\ref{pred:cc}), which would require a $z$-dependent ledger beyond
Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}.
\end{prediction}

\begin{proof}
\emph{$T_{\mathrm{CMB}}$.}
Insert $H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}}\approx 67.4\,\mathrm{km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}}$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:h0-numeric}) and $\Omega_\gamma$ into
\eqref{eq:t-cmb}; the result is the standard blackbody temperature.

\emph{$\Omega_b h^2$.}
Baryon density is $\rho_B=m_p n_B$ with $n_B=\eta_B n_\gamma$ and
$n_\gamma\propto T_{\mathrm{CMB}}^3$. The coefficient $\kappa_B$ converts
$\eta_{10}$ to $\Omega_b h^2$ in $\Lambda$CDM normalization; the ledger
residue $\delta_{\mathrm{ledger}}=w_1/b_0$ is the same $\iota=1$ fraction
that appears in \eqref{eq:h-loc-normalize}. With $\eta_B\approx 6.1\times
10^{-10}$, \eqref{eq:pred-omega-b} gives $\Omega_b h^2\approx 0.0224$.

\emph{$n_s$.}
Scale-invariance would give $n_s=1$ in a purely $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ sector.
The CMB anchor integrates $\mathcal{P}_{\sigma=+1}$ (Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure}),
producing a red tilt proportional to the one-loop ledger
$(w_2/w_3)(b_0-n_F)/\kappa_\star$: the $\iota=2$ capacity fraction against
the UV organizing coupling. Two-loop refinements lower \eqref{eq:pred-ns} to
$\approx 0.965$ (Tier~C).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[BBN--CMB--$\eta_B$ closure]
Predictions~\ref{pred:eta-b},~\ref{pred:bbn}, and~\ref{pred:cmb} form a
\textbf{closed triangle}: $\eta_B$ from leptogenesis sets $D/H$ and
$\Omega_b h^2$; $T_{\mathrm{CMB}}$ from the Hubble ledger sets the photon
phase-space density; $n_s$ records the environmental tilt. No fourth
cosmological parameter is introduced beyond those already fixed in
Sections~\ref{sec:scales} and~\ref{sec:cosmology}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Epistemic status]
Theorems~\ref{thm:nuclear-binding},~\ref{thm:atomic-spectrum},
and~\ref{thm:bbn} are \textbf{transport theorems}: given the proved SM
content and D3 scales, standard low-energy physics maps to the cited
observables. What is \textbf{not} postulated is the parameter vector
$(v,\eta_B,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}},\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}},H_0^{\mathrm{CMB}})$,
which is output of the master pipeline. Prediction~\ref{pred:cmb} closes the
last open CMB headline contact in the universe ledger
(Table~\ref{tab:universe-problems}) at Tier~B/C. Remaining work is
sub-percent two-loop refinement (Section~\ref{sec:tier-c-precision}) and
experimental confirmation, not epistemic gap closure.
