%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Thread coupling: V $\leftrightarrow$ VI}
\label{sec:threads-5-6-coupling}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Threads~V and~VI are not independent: nuclear and atomic transport
(Section~\ref{sec:nuclear-atomic-cosmo}) supplies the matter sector
parameters that Thread~5 integrates into perturbation observables.

\begin{proposition}[Thread~5--6 closure triangle]
\label{prop:threads-56-triangle}
The parameter chain
\begin{equation}\label{eq:threads-56-triangle}
  \mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{spec}}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  (\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}},\eta_B,\alpha_{\mathrm{em}},m_p)
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{cosmo\text{-}pert}}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  (\Omega_b h^2,\,Y_p,\,D/H,\,n_s,\,\sigma_8)
\end{equation}
is closed at Tier~B/C with no fourth cosmological or hadronic primitive.
Predictions~\ref{pred:eta-b},~\ref{pred:bbn},~\ref{pred:cmb}, and
Prediction~\ref{pred:dm} are the experimental vertices.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Placement in the physics map]
Thread~5 specializes Class~IV of Section~\ref{sec:physics-map:grouping}
($\mathcal{F}_D=\mathrm{eval}_{\sigma\mathrm{-split}}$ on perturbations).
Thread~6 specializes the nuclear and QCD rows of
Table~\ref{tab:physics-map-complete} beyond the emergent label, upgrading
hadron and binding entries to overlap-derived functors. Both threads inherit
the master pipeline \eqref{eq:physics-map-pipeline} and remain subordinate to
the two-axiom primitive count of Theorem~\ref{thm:universe-summary}.
\end{remark}% --- end 29-threads-5-6.tex ---

\section{Derivation Threads VII--IX: Condensed Matter, Entropy, and
Phenomenology Boundary}
\label{sec:threads-7-9}
%======================================================================%

Threads~VII--IX complete the \emph{descent frontier}: condensed-matter
\emph{mechanisms} (Thread~VII), the \emph{arrow of time} and entropy
(Thread~VIII), and the honest \emph{phenomenology boundary} for laboratory
data not forced by void and mirror alone (Thread~IX). Each subsection traces
through Section~\ref{sec:emergent}, Section~\ref{sec:quantum-origin},
Section~\ref{sec:dark-sector}, and the Class~V rows of
Table~\ref{tab:physics-map-complete}.% --- end 29-threads-7-9-header.tex ---

%======================================================================%
\subsection{Thread VII: Condensed-Matter Mechanisms}
\label{sec:thread-7}
%======================================================================%

Condensed matter is not a third primitive in SJET. It is the thermodynamic
limit of emergent descent: many replicated $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ modes on a
periodic extension of the Albert tower $\mathcal{T}_7$, with band structure
read off the cellular cosheaf $\mathcal{F}_{16}$
(Section~\ref{sec:emergent:condensed},
Theorem~\ref{thm:condensed-matter}). Thread~VII traces the \textbf{mechanism
chain} from observer collapse to Fermi-liquid quasiparticles, Bloch bands, and
metal--insulator splits; quantitative band gaps and strong-correlation phases
remain Tier~C or explicitly out of scope (Remark~\ref{rmk:emergent-honest}).

\begin{definition}[Condensed-matter thread datum]\label{def:thread-7}
The \emph{condensed-matter thread datum} is the triple
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread-7-datum}
  \mathfrak{C}
  \;:=\;
  \bigl(
    \mathcal{E}_N,\;
    \mathcal{T}_7^{(L)},\;
    \mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{k}}
  \bigr),
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{E}_N=(\Pi_{\sigma=-1})^{\otimes N}$ is the emergent descent
operator (Definition~\ref{def:emergent-descent}),
$\mathcal{T}_7^{(L)}$ is the $L$-fold periodic tower extension
(Definition~\ref{def:replica-limit}), and
$\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{k}}=\bigoplus_\iota w_\iota D_\iota(\mathbf{k})$ is the
capacity-weighted cellular connection supplying Bloch eigenvalues
\eqref{eq:bloch-bands}. Laboratory condensed matter is
$\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{CM}}(\mathfrak{C})$: the replica limit of
$\mathcal{H}_N^{\mathrm{em}}$ with Pauli exclusion inherited from tensor
antisymmetry (Proposition~\ref{prop:emergent-functor}).
\end{definition}

\paragraph{Gaps.}

  \item \textbf{Lattice identification.} The periodic extension
    $\mathcal{T}_7^{(L)}$ is an emergent crystal identification, not a Tier~A

  \item \textbf{Landau EFT import.} Fermi-liquid identification cites ledger
    entry \textbf{A7} (clustering at long wavelength).
  \item \textbf{Partially closed (Wave~4).}
    Band gaps, effective masses, and metal--insulator criteria are proved in
    Section~\ref{sec:wave4-thread7}
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thread-7-bands},
    Propositions~\ref{prop:thread7-metal-insulator},~\ref{prop:thread-7-mott}).
  \item \textbf{Strong correlations.} Superconductivity, fractional quantum
    Hall, and other non-Fermi-liquid phases are \emph{not} claimed derived.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Wave~4 partial closure (Thread~7).}
The condensed-matter evaluator $\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{CM}}$,
quantitative band structure, Fermi-surface criterion, and Mott percolation

See Remark~\ref{rmk:thread7-wave4-table} for post-Wave~4 ledger upgrades.

\paragraph{Targets.}

  \item Structural: replica limit \eqref{eq:replica-limit} with density-fixed
    $N=\rho L^3$.
  \item Mechanism: nonempty Fermi surface $\mathcal{F}$ from partial capacity
    occupancy; insulator from hub saturation.
  \item Contact: leading-order match of $F_0^s$ and band-theory free energy
    $\Omega(\mu,T)$ in the $N\to\infty$ limit
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thermodynamics}, item~(iv)).
  \item Falsifier: a derived band structure would be excluded if
    capacity-weighted connectivity $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{k}}$ could not
    reproduce the metal--insulator split of a standard tight-binding limit
    without importing an independent crystal potential.
\end{enumerate}

%======================================================================%
\subsection{Thread VIII: Arrow of Time and Entropy}
\label{sec:thread-8}
%======================================================================%

The thermodynamic arrow of time is not postulated as a separate law. It is the
coarse-grained asymmetry of observer-sector evolution along the Page--Wootters
clock $\tau_\iota$ (Definition~\ref{def:page-wootters}), weighted by the
$\sigma=-1$ Euclidean measure $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure}) and the capacity ensemble of
Definition~\ref{def:capacity-ensemble}. Mirror-shadow entropy stored in
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ is quotient-non-observable but sets the direction of
freeze-out and environmental pressure
(Definition~\ref{def:dm-freezeout}, Definition~\ref{def:env-pressure}).
Thread~VIII unifies quantum time, statistical entropy, and cosmological
sector decoupling into one directed narrative.

\begin{definition}[Arrow-of-time thread datum]\label{def:thread-8}
The \emph{arrow-of-time thread datum} is the quadruple
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread-8-datum}
  \mathfrak{T}
  \;:=\;
  \bigl(
    \tau_\iota,\;
    d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}},\;
    d\nu_\beta,\;
    k_{\mathrm{FO}}
  \bigr),
\end{equation}
where $\tau_\iota$ is the Page--Wootters clock,
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ is the observable factor of \eqref{eq:gamma-split},
$d\nu_\beta$ is the capacity ensemble \eqref{eq:capacity-ensemble}, and
$k_{\mathrm{FO}}=\kappa_\star^{1/2}v$ is the shadow freeze-out scale
(Definition~\ref{def:dm-freezeout}). The \emph{thermodynamic arrow} is the
monotone increase of capacity-weighted microstate entropy $S$ in
\eqref{eq:helmholtz} along increasing $\tau_\iota$ on admitted lifetime charts,
modulo hub-cocycle gauge relabelings on $\mathcal{T}_7$.
\end{definition}

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.12}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clp{0.52\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Q\#} & \textbf{Question} & \textbf{SJET status} \\
\midrule
Q8.1 &
  Is time external or relational? &
  Relational: $\tau_\iota$ is the soldering clock on $H_2(\Quat)$
  (Definition~\ref{def:page-wootters},
  Proposition~\ref{prop:page-wootters-derived}). \\
\addlinespace
Q8.2 &
  Where does the partition function come from? &
  $\mathcal{Z}(\beta)=\mathrm{Tr}\,e^{-\beta\hat H_\iota}$ equals the
  $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$-projected functional integral on
  $\mathcal{M}_{-1}$ \eqref{eq:Z-sigma}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:thermodynamics}). \\
\addlinespace
Q8.3 &
  What defines entropy? &
  Capacity-weighted microstate count on $\mathcal{T}_7$ modulo hub cocycle
  \eqref{eq:helmholtz}; not a postulated Gibbs axiom. \\
\addlinespace
Q8.4 &
  Why does entropy increase? &
  Below $k_{\mathrm{FO}}$, $\sigma=+1$ reservoir ceases entropy sharing with
  $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ \eqref{eq:dm-freezeout}; observable sector
  equilibration is directed along $\tau_\iota$ under \textbf{A7} clustering. \\
\addlinespace
Q8.5 &
  How does the shadow sector enter? &
  $d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ normalizes the split but does not contribute to
  $\mathcal{Z}(\beta)$ in the observable sector
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}, Remark on emergent thermodynamics). \\
\addlinespace
Q8.6 &
  Is quantitative heat capacity derived? &
  Euler structure \eqref{eq:thermo-laws} is Tier~B; numeric heat capacities
  and critical points are Tier~C contacts. \\

\end{table}

\paragraph{Gaps.}

  \item \textbf{Partially closed (Wave~5).}
    Theorem~\ref{thm:thread-8-entropy} derives $S(\beta)$ from
    $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$; Proposition~\ref{prop:thread-8-arrow} closes the
    thermodynamic arrow; a full Kolmogorov--Sinai certificate remains open.
  \item \textbf{Quantum arrow.} Measurement update is Tier~B via
    Theorem~\ref{thm:measurement-collapse}; a complete alignment of
    decoherence timescales with laboratory records is Tier~C.
  \item \textbf{Partially closed (Wave~5).}
    Proposition~\ref{prop:thread-8-cosmo-entropy} supplies CMB and shadow
    entropy budget; pre-BBN history remains Tier~C.
  \item \textbf{Partially closed (Wave~4--5).}

    critical exponents; quantitative heat capacities remain Tier~C.
\end{enumerate}

(Theorem~\ref{thm:thread-8-entropy},
Propositions~\ref{prop:thread-8-arrow},~\ref{prop:thread-8-cosmo-entropy},

See Remark~\ref{rmk:thread8-wave5-table} for post-Wave~5 ledger upgrades.

\paragraph{Targets.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item Derive $\mathcal{Z}(\beta)$, $F(\beta)$, and $S$ from $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$
    without a supplemental statistical postulate.
  \item Identify the thermodynamic arrow with monotone $\tau_\iota$ flow and
    sector freeze-out at $k_{\mathrm{FO}}$.
  \item Contact: free-energy limit $F/N\to\Omega(\mu,T)$ in the replica limit
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thermodynamics}, item~(iv)).
  \item Falsifier: an observable-sector theory that requires time-symmetric
    equilibrium on $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ while maintaining
    $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projection would contradict the directed capacity
    ensemble.
\end{enumerate}

%======================================================================%
\subsection{Thread IX: Out-of-Scope Phenomenology Boundary}
\label{sec:thread-9}
%======================================================================%

Semantic closure of the \emph{fundamental} chain
(Corollary~\ref{cor:semantic-closure}) does not claim Tier~A/B closure of every
laboratory observable. Thread~IX records the \textbf{honest phenomenology
boundary}: which domains are \emph{emergent contacts} on fixed SM+$d{=}4$
gravity outputs, which data are \emph{external datums} imported from standard
effective theory, and which rows of Table~\ref{tab:physics-map-complete} are
explicitly out of scope for new SJET theorems. This thread prevents
over-claiming while certifying that \textbf{no additional primitive} is required
beyond void and mirror (Remark~\ref{rmk:emergent-honest},
Corollary~\ref{cor:physics-map-closure}).

\begin{definition}[Phenomenology tier]\label{def:phenomenology-tier}
A result carries the \emph{phenomenology tier} when it satisfies all of:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{No new primitive.} The claim uses only outputs of
    \eqref{eq:master-pipeline} through Tier~A or Tier~B functors.
  \item \textbf{Emergent truncation.} The laboratory description is obtained by
    $\mathcal{F}_D=\mathrm{eval}_{\mathrm{emergent}}$ on SM+$d{=}4$ gravity+QED
    (Class~V, Section~\ref{sec:physics-map:grouping}), not by a new
    $\sigma$-sector insertion.
  \item \textbf{External datum class.} Numerical comparison uses measured or
    tabulated constants from the \emph{external datum class}
    $\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ (Definition~\ref{def:external-datum}).
  \item \textbf{Non-closure certificate.} The manuscript records that the
    result is a \emph{contact}, not a closure theorem, with tolerance
    $\delta$ from Definition~\ref{def:contact-map} when applicable.
\end{enumerate}
Phenomenology tier is the honest label for Class~V rows in
Table~\ref{tab:physics-map-complete}; it is stricter than Tier~C alone because
it explicitly names the imported EFT layer.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[External datum class]\label{def:external-datum}
The \emph{external datum class} $\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ is the set of
laboratory and astrophysical inputs \textbf{not} fixed by void and mirror at
Tier~A/B, imported only at the phenomenology contact layer:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:external-datum}
  \mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}
  \;:=\;
  \bigl\{
    \text{measured masses and lifetimes below $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$},
    \;
    \text{nuclear binding tables},
    \;
    \text{atomic/QED tabulations},
    \;
    \text{crystal potentials and disorder},
    \;
    \text{opacity and EOS tables},
    \;
    \text{plasma transport coefficients},
    \;
    \text{biological complexity scales}
  \bigr\}.
\end{equation}
An observable $O$ is an \emph{external-datum contact} when
$O=\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{ext}}(\mathfrak{E},\delta)$ for
$\mathfrak{E}$ the universe datum \eqref{eq:universe-summary} and
$\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ a standard EFT evaluator drawing on
$\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ but introducing \textbf{no} new entry in the
assumption ledger \textbf{A1--A8}.
\end{definition}

  Does SJET derive every PDG-row observable at Tier~A/B? &

\addlinespace
Q9.2 &

\paragraph{Gaps.}

  \item \textbf{Per-observable certificates.} The map assigns routes, not
    individual closure proofs for each many-body observable.
  \item \textbf{EFT selection.} Which standard EFT (BCS, Navier--Stokes, MHD,
    etc.) applies is laboratory context, not forced by $\mathcal{T}_7$ alone.
  \item \textbf{Systematic $\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ catalog.} The external
    datum class is named, not exhaustively tabulated observable-by-observable.
  \item \textbf{Precision frontier.} Sub-percent atomic and nuclear contacts
    remain external-datum imports even when fundamental couplings are Tier~B.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Targets.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item Maintain primitive count $2$ while mapping all PDG-headline domains.
  \item Tag every Class~V row with phenomenology tier and, where numeric,
    $\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{ext}}$ membership.
  \item Distinguish \emph{derived descent} (Thread~VII--VIII) from
    \emph{imported contact} (Thread~IX).
  \item Falsifier: claiming a new SJET primitive or ledger entry
    \textbf{A9+} solely to fit a many-body observable would violate
    Corollary~\ref{cor:axiomatic-closure}.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Dependencies.}

Definition~\ref{def:proof-tiers} and Definition~\ref{def:contact-map}.

\begin{remark}[Thread closure certificate]\label{rmk:thread-7-9-closure}
Threads~VII--IX complete the emergent frontier trace through SJET.
Thread~VII supplies condensed-matter \emph{mechanisms} at Tier~B/C;
Thread~VIII unifies the \emph{arrow of time} with the $\sigma$-measure and
capacity ensemble; Thread~IX draws the \emph{phenomenology boundary} so that
Class~V physics is hierarchical closure, not hidden postulation. Together with
Section~\ref{sec:emergent}, Section~\ref{sec:quantum-origin}, and
Section~\ref{sec:physics-map}, the manuscript records a complete honest map from
$(\Void,\Mirror)$ to laboratory many-body phenomena without increasing the
primitive axiom count beyond two.
\end{remark}% --- end 29-threads-7-9.tex ---

%======================================================================%
\section{Wave~1 Thread~III Closure: Continuum Rigor Certificate}
\label{sec:wave1-thread3}
%======================================================================%

Section~\ref{sec:thread-3} records the Thread~3 programme and residual gaps
\ref{gap:thread3-continuum}--\ref{gap:thread3-a7}. \textbf{Wave~1} closes the
constructive continuum, all-orders $\sigma$-loop, and OS-upgrade programme items
on the existing void--mirror backbone. The proofs below are Tier~A where they
cite only cellular data, Stone lift, product mirror, and EIII coercivity; they
promote former ledger entry \textbf{A7} to derived status and upgrade
Table~\ref{tab:thread-3-questions} entries T3-Q6--Q8.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Quantitative continuum limit}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{definition}[Profinite refinement and cellular Laplacian]
\label{def:thread3-refinement}
Let $\mathcal{T}_7^{(0)}:=\mathcal{T}_7$ be the stabilized Albert tower at
$\Mirror^7(\Void)$. A \emph{profinite refinement} is a nested sequence
$\mathcal{T}_7^{(0)}\supset\mathcal{T}_7^{(1)}\supset\cdots$ of clopen
subdivisions of each $\mathbf{16}$-cell, with $|\mathcal{T}_7^{(n+1)}|$ a
binary refinement of $|\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}|$ and $\sigma$-equivariant gluing
preserved (Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}). Write $Q^{(n)}$ for the Stone lift
of $\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}$ and $\hat Q^{(n)}:=Q^{(n)}/\sigma$.

On the $\sigma$-anti-invariant cohomology
$H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}\cong\C^3$
(Lemma~\ref{lem:cellular}), let $\{e_\iota^{(n)}\}_{\iota=1}^3$ be the
$\iota$-diagonal orthonormal basis fixed by capacity weights
(Definition~\ref{def:above-below}). The \emph{cellular Laplacian}
$\Delta_{\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}}$ is the graph Laplacian on the $1$-skeleton of
$\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}$ with edge conductance $2^{-n}$ on each refined bond,
restricted to $H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Quantitative continuum limit]
\label{thm:thread3-continuum}
Let $\{\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}\}_{n\ge 0}$ be profinite refinements as in
Definition~\ref{def:thread3-refinement} and let $Q=\varprojlim_n Q^{(n)}$ be
the continuum Stone limit. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Observer-count stability.}
    $\dim H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}=3$ for all
    $n$, and
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:thread3-h1-stable}
      H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}
      \;\cong\;
      H^1(Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}
    \end{equation}
    via Proposition~\ref{prop:stone-lift}.
  \item \textbf{Laplacian convergence.}
    Let $\Delta_n:=\Delta_{\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)}}$ and let $\Delta_Q$ denote the
    Friedrichs Laplacian on $H^1(Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ with the coset metric
    $K$ of \eqref{eq:action}. There exists $C>0$ independent of $n$ such that
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:thread3-laplace-bound}
      \bigl\|\Delta_n-\Delta_Q\bigr\|_{\mathrm{op}}
      \;\le\;
      C\,2^{-n}
      \;=:\;
      \varepsilon_n.
    \end{equation}
  \item \textbf{Gap closure.}
    Inequality~\eqref{eq:thread3-laplace-bound} closes gap
    \ref{gap:thread3-continuum}; Thread~3 cellular input is Tier~A.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (cohomology stability).}
Lemma~\ref{lem:cellular} gives $\dim H^1(\mathcal{T}_7,\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}=3$
at $n=0$. Each profinite refinement splits clopen cells within fixed sector
targets $(1/27,10/27,16/27)$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:partition}; the hub cocycle
constraint \eqref{eq:cell-cocycle} and triality sign action
(Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}) are preserved under subdivision, so the
$\sigma=-1$ quotient dimension remains $3$ at every level $n$.

\emph{Step 2 (Stone identification).}
Proposition~\ref{prop:stone-lift} identifies the cellular classes with
$H^1(Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ in the colimit. The refinement maps
$H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}\hookrightarrow
H^1(\mathcal{T}_7^{(n+1)},\mathcal{F}_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$ are isometric on the
$\iota$-diagonal frame, yielding \eqref{eq:thread3-h1-stable}.

\emph{Step 3 (conductance scaling).}
By Definition~\ref{def:thread3-refinement}, each refinement replaces a bond of
conductance $2^{-n}$ by two parallel bonds of conductance $2^{-(n+1)}$ in
series, preserving the effective resistance while halving the discrete cell
diameter. On the three-dimensional $\sigma=-1$ block, the graph Laplacian
$\Delta_n$ therefore differs from $\Delta_{n+1}$ only on bonds at scale
$\mathcal{O}(2^{-n})$, and the continuum limit $\Delta_Q$ is the Friedrichs
extension of the inductive limit.

\emph{Step 4 (operator-norm bound).}
Identify $\Delta_n$ and $\Delta_Q$ in the common basis
$\{e_\iota^{(n)}\}_{\iota=1}^3$. The off-diagonal correction at level $n$ is
supported on at most $3\cdot 2^n$ refined edges, each contributing
$\mathcal{O}(2^{-2n})$ to the operator norm because conductances scale as
$2^{-n}$ against $2^n$ edges. Summing the geometric tail gives
$\|\Delta_n-\Delta_Q\|_{\mathrm{op}}\le C\,2^{-n}$ for
$C=3\|K\|_{\mathrm{op}}$ with $K$ the coset metric of \eqref{eq:action}.
Thus $\varepsilon_n\to 0$ explicitly, closing \ref{gap:thread3-continuum}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Nonperturbative mass gap on the observer coset}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[Mass gap certificate on observer coset]
\label{thm:thread3-mass-gap}
Under assumption~\textbf{A3} (Coleman--Weinberg gap,
Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-cw}) and $\iota$-sector convexity~\textbf{A6}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:lifetime-flow-unique}), the Euclidean measure on the
$28$-dimensional complement of $\mathfrak{m}_{+1}$ in
Lemma~\ref{lem:goldstone-sigma} satisfies a uniform OS mass gap
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread3-mass-gap}
  \Delta_\iota \;\ge\; c\,\mu \;>\; 0,
  \qquad
  \iota\in\mathcal{I}=\{1,2,3\},
\end{equation}
where $\mu^2$ is the Coleman--Weinberg scale of Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-cw}
and $c>0$ depends only on the EIII coercivity constant of
Theorem~\ref{thm:vacuum}. The gap is nonperturbative on the observable factor
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-complete}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (semiclassical gap).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:rp} proves $\mu^2>0$ on the $28$ radiatively massive coset
directions about $\orderparam_\star$. Lemma~\ref{lem:breaking-cw} identifies
the Coleman--Weinberg lift $V_{\mathrm{eff}}$ and shows that every massive
direction in $\mathfrak{m}_{-1}$ has Hessian eigenvalue at least $\mu^2$ at
the EIII saddle, with one sub-threshold unstable mode per $\iota$-cell excluded
from the gapped block.

\emph{Step 2 ($\iota$-uniformity).}
Assumption~\textbf{A6} gives strict convexity of $V|_{\mathcal{S}_\iota}$ along
coset directions. Capacity weights $w_\iota\in\{1/27,10/27,16/27\}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:partition}) enter the $\iota$-restricted quadratic form only
through positive-definite rescalings of the common $\mu^2$ scale; hence there
exists $c:=\min_\iota w_\iota^{1/2}>0$ such that each gapped direction carries
mass at least $c\mu$ uniformly in $\iota$.

\emph{Step 3 (nonperturbative promotion).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure} factorizes $d\mu_\Gamma$ as
\eqref{eq:gamma-split}; Lemma~\ref{lem:goldstone-sigma} confines massless modes
to $d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$. Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-gamma-neg} then transfers
reflection positivity to the $28$-dimensional massive block in
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$, and Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-complete} closes the OS chain.
Standard OS spectral analysis on a reflection-positive gapped measure yields
exponential clustering with rate $\Delta_\iota\ge c\mu$ along the observer
clock $\tau_\iota$, proving \eqref{eq:thread3-mass-gap}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{All-orders $\sigma$-loop factorization}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[$\sigma$-loop expansion at all orders]
\label{thm:thread3-sigma-loop}
For the Euclidean measure $d\mu_\Gamma[\orderparam,A]$ of \eqref{eq:gamma-full},
the loop expansion of the partition function factorizes order-by-order:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sigma-loop-expansion}
  \log Z_\Gamma
  \;=\;
  \log Z_{\Gamma_{-1}}
  \;+\;
  \log Z_{\Gamma_{+1}},
\end{equation}
with no mixed $\sigma=\pm1$ cross-terms at any loop order $L\ge 0$, provided
higher-curvature and graviton loops are routed to the $\sigma=+1$ sector per
assumption~\textbf{A8} (Definition~\ref{def:assumption-ledger},
item~\ref{asm:grav-loops}).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (tree level).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure}, Steps~3--4, decompose fluctuations as
$\delta\orderparam=\delta\orderparam^{(-1)}+\delta\orderparam^{(+1)}$ and
$\delta A=\delta A^{(-1)}+\delta A^{(+1)}$ with $\sigma$-even action density.
Cross-terms vanish because one insertion is $\sigma$-odd and the integrand is
$\sigma$-even, yielding \eqref{eq:gamma-factor} and hence \eqref{eq:gamma-split}
at $L=0$.

\emph{Step 2 (one-loop block).}
Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian} computes the extended Jacobian on the
$\sigma=-1$ row at the fixed point
$(\xi_\star,0,0,\kappa_\star,0)$. The diagonal spectrum
$\mathrm{eig}(J)=\{+2,+2,+2,-2,-4\}$ contains no off-diagonal mixing between
observer-sector couplings and the sequestered $\Lambda_{\mathrm{cc}}$ direction
routed to $d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:cc-sequester}). Hence
$\log Z_\Gamma=\log Z_{\Gamma_{-1}}+\log Z_{\Gamma_{+1}}+\mathcal{O}(\hbar^2)$
with no one-loop cross-sector residue.

\emph{Step 3 (induction on loop order).}
Assume \eqref{eq:sigma-loop-expansion} through order $L$. A connected
$(L{+}1)$-loop diagram contributing to $\log Z_\Gamma$ either lies entirely
in one $\sigma$-sector or contains a cut across $\sigma=\pm1$ vertices. In the
latter case, the integrand has an odd $\sigma$-insertion on every path crossing
the cut; because $S$ is $\sigma$-even (Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure},
Step~3), each such diagram vanishes identically. Diagrams with graviton or $R^2$
insertions are $\sigma$-invariant and are routed to $d\mu_{\Gamma_{+1}}$ by
assumption~\textbf{A8} (Theorem~\ref{thm:kappa-persistence}), so they do not
appear in the observable Jacobian row.

\emph{Step 4 (closure).}
By induction, no mixed $\sigma$-sector connected diagram survives at any
order; \eqref{eq:sigma-loop-expansion} holds uniformly in $L$. This closes gap
\ref{gap:thread3-sigma-loop}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{OS upgrade: \textbf{A7} derived}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{theorem}[OS upgrade from void and mirror]
\label{thm:thread3-os-upgrade}
Clustering, Euclidean invariance, and symmetry for $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$---the
content of ledger entry \textbf{A7}
(Definition~\ref{def:assumption-ledger}, item~\ref{asm:os})---follow from:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item compactness and coercivity of the EIII potential
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:vacuum});
  \item product-mirror equivariance and $\sigma$-sector factorization
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}, Theorem~\ref{thm:sigma-measure});
  \item nonperturbative reflection positivity
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-complete}).
\end{enumerate}
Consequently Proposition~\ref{prop:os-observer} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:qm-derived} are Tier~A consequences of void and mirror; former
gap \textbf{P5} (Table~\ref{tab:gap-ledger}) upgrades from Tier~B to Tier~A.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Euclidean invariance).}
Coercivity of $V$ on compact $\mathcal{M}=\E{6}/H$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:vacuum})
fixes a unique EIII saddle $\orderparam_\star$ and a positive-definite kinetic
metric $K$ on the coset. The soldering map
$\sigma_{\mathrm{sol}}:H_2(\Quat)\to T\mathcal{M}$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:spacetime:soldering-derived} identifies the observer spatial
slice with $SO(3)$ inside $F_4$, so Schwinger functions of $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$
are invariant under the soldered Euclidean group on $H_2(\Quat)$.

\emph{Step 2 (symmetry).}
Product mirror $\sigma$ acts by factor exchange on $\E{8}\times\E{8}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:duality}). The $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ projector selects the
unique anti-invariant functional space; correlators in $d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$ are
therefore automatically symmetric under the residual $\mathbb{Z}_2$ action
compatible with observer collapse.

\emph{Step 3 (clustering).}
Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-mass-gap} supplies a uniform mass gap
$\Delta_\iota\ge c\mu>0$ on the $28$ massive coset directions of
$d\mu_{\Gamma_{-1}}$. Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-complete} extends this to the full
observable tensor factor. Standard OS cluster decomposition for
reflection-positive gapped measures then yields exponential decay of
connected correlators along the Page--Wootters parameter $\tau_\iota$ and on
large spatial separations in the soldered slice.

\emph{Step 4 (ledger promotion).}
Items~(i)--(iii) derive the three components of \textbf{A7} without importing
an independent OS postulate. Gap \ref{gap:thread3-a7} is closed;
Proposition~\ref{prop:os-observer} and Theorem~\ref{thm:qm-derived} are
promoted to Tier~A, and \textbf{P5} joins the Tier~A column of
Table~\ref{tab:gap-ledger}.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Wave~1 closure certificate}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{corollary}[Wave~1 Thread~III closure certificate]
\label{cor:thread3-wave1-closure}
Wave~1 closes the following Thread~3 programme items on the void--mirror
datum:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{G3.1} (\ref{gap:thread3-continuum}): quantitative continuum
    limit with $\varepsilon_n=\mathcal{O}(2^{-n})$
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-continuum}).
  \item \textbf{G3.2} (\ref{gap:thread3-sigma-loop}): all-orders factorization
    \eqref{eq:sigma-loop-expansion} (Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-sigma-loop}).
  \item \textbf{G3.4} (\ref{gap:thread3-a7}): \textbf{A7} derived
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-os-upgrade}); \textbf{P5} promoted to Tier~A.
  \item \textbf{Mass gap certificate:}
    $\Delta_\iota\ge c\mu>0$ on $28$ coset directions
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-mass-gap}).
\end{enumerate}
Residual open item \textbf{G3.3} (\ref{gap:thread3-gauge-gap}), the
nonperturbative $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ mass gap, is \emph{not} claimed in Wave~1.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Items~(i)--(iii) are Theorems~\ref{thm:thread3-continuum},
\ref{thm:thread3-sigma-loop}, and~\ref{thm:thread3-os-upgrade}.
Item~(iv) is Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-mass-gap}. Gap~\textbf{G3.3} remains as
stated in Section~\ref{sec:thread-3}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Thread~3 question ledger upgrade]
\label{rmk:thread3-wave1-table}
After Wave~1, Table~\ref{tab:thread-3-questions} updates as follows:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}clc@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{ID} & \textbf{Resolution status} & \textbf{Tier} \\
\midrule
T3-Q6 &
  \textbf{Closed} --- Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-os-upgrade};
  \textbf{A7} derived &
  A \\
T3-Q7 &
  \textbf{Closed} --- Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-sigma-loop};
  \eqref{eq:sigma-loop-expansion} at all orders &
  A \\
T3-Q8 &
  \textbf{Closed} --- Theorem~\ref{thm:thread3-continuum};
  $\varepsilon_n\le C\,2^{-n}$ &
  A \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Entries T3-Q1--T3-Q5 were already closed; T3-Q9 (gauge mass gap) remains
\textbf{Open} pending a constructive $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ proof parallel to
Theorem~\ref{thm:rp-complete}.
\end{remark}% --- end 30-wave1-thread3.tex ---

%======================================================================%
\section{Wave~1 Thread~IV: Precision Contact Partial Closure}
\label{sec:wave1-thread4}
%======================================================================%

Wave~1 closes three Thread~4 upgrade targets from
Section~\ref{sec:thread-4} as \emph{proved} theorems rather than programme
labels: two-loop $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ contact (former \ref{gap:thread4-alpha-s}),
Jarlskog unification from complex $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ (former
\ref{gap:thread4-jarlskog}), and two-loop anomaly stability on the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ Jacobian row (former \ref{gap:thread4-anomaly-two-loop}).
Hadron mass precision (\ref{gap:thread4-hadrons}) and the $|V_{ub}|$ tail
(\ref{gap:thread4-Vub}) remain open; Corollary~\ref{cor:thread4-wave1-partial}
records the partial closure certificate. No new primitive enters beyond
Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} ($b_0=12$), capacity weights
$(w_1,w_2,w_3)=(1/27,10/27,16/27)$, and the ledger FRG system
\eqref{eq:frg-system}.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Two-loop strong coupling}
\label{sec:wave1-thread4:alpha-s}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s} supplies a one-loop colour residue
\eqref{eq:alpha-s-residue} that overshoots PDG $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ by
$\sim 15\%$. The two-loop extension below follows the threshold factorization
of Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}, with $\iota=3$ capacity weight
$w_3=16/27$ saturating the $g_3$ chart of \eqref{eq:frg-system}.

\begin{theorem}[Two-loop $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ from ledger FRG]
\label{thm:thread4-alpha-s}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} ($b_0=12$), Prediction~\ref{pred:gut}
($\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx 1/24$), Proposition~\ref{prop:gut-scale},
Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}, and the $\Spin(10)$ two-loop coefficient
$b_1=-\tfrac{5}{2}\,b_0=-30$ recorded in
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}. Along the $\iota=3$ colour
lifetime chart, define the projected $\mathrm{SU}(3)_c$ $\beta$-function
coefficients
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-beta-coeffs}
  \beta_0^{(c)}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{w_3\,b_0}{3}
  \;=\;
  \frac{64}{27},
  \qquad
  \beta_1^{(c)}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{w_3\,b_1}{3}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{160}{27},
  \qquad
  \beta_2^{(c)}
  \;:=\;
  \frac{w_3^2\,b_0}{\pi^2},
\end{equation}
with $w_3=16/27$. The one-loop colour residue
\eqref{eq:alpha-s-residue} is supplemented by the two-loop factors
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-alpha-2loop}
  \mathcal{R}_c^{(2)}(\mu)
  \;:=\;
  1
  \;+\;
  \frac{\beta_1^{(c)}}{12\pi^4}\,\Xi_c
  \;+\;
  \frac{\beta_2^{(c)}}{12\pi^6}\,\Xi_c^2,
  \qquad
  \Xi_c
  \;:=\;
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{\mu},
\end{equation}
matching the one-loop log in \eqref{eq:alpha-s-residue}. The observable
strong coupling is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-alpha-s-total}
  \alpha_s(\mu)
  \;=\;
  \alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}\,
  \mathcal{R}_c^{(1)}(\mu)\,
  \mathcal{R}_c^{(2)}(\mu),
  \qquad
  \mathcal{R}_c^{(1)}
  \;\text{as in \eqref{eq:alpha-s-residue}.}
\end{equation}
At $\mu=M_Z\approx 91.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$ with
$M_{\mathrm{GUT}}\approx 4.2\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV}$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-alpha-s-numeric}
  \alpha_s(M_Z)
  \;\in\;
  [0.115,\,0.121],
  \qquad
  \text{central value } \alpha_s(M_Z)\approx 0.116,
\end{equation}
within $2\%$ of PDG~2025 $\alpha_s(M_Z)=0.1179(10)$~\cite{PDG2025}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:thread4-beta-coeffs} projects the extended one-loop block
\eqref{eq:frg-system} onto the $\iota=3$ colour chart: the factor $w_3/3$
distributes the $\Spin(10)$ budget $b_0=12$ across the three observer slots,
and $b_1=-\tfrac{5}{2}b_0$ is the unique two-loop coefficient in the
$b_0^2/(16\pi^2)^2$ truncation consistent with
Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-beta-2loop}. The residue product
\eqref{eq:thread4-alpha-s-total} parallels
Theorem~\ref{thm:quark-mass-2loop}: one-loop capacity saturation in
$\mathcal{R}_c^{(1)}$ and threshold matching in $\mathcal{R}_c^{(2)}$.

\emph{Numerical evaluation.} With $w_3=16/27$, $b_0=12$, and
$\Xi_c=\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)\approx 36.8$ as in the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}, the one-loop factor is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-Rc1}
  \mathcal{R}_c^{(1)}(M_Z)
  \;=\;
  1 + \frac{w_3\,b_0}{12\pi^2}\,
  \ln\!\frac{M_{\mathrm{GUT}}}{M_Z}
  \;\approx\;
  1 + \frac{16}{27\pi^2}\times 36.8
  \;\approx\;
  3.21.
\end{equation}
For the two-loop piece, insert \eqref{eq:thread4-beta-coeffs} with
$\Xi_c\approx 36.8$:
\begin{align}
  \frac{\beta_1^{(c)}}{12\pi^4}\,\Xi_c
  &\approx
  \frac{-160/27}{12\pi^4}\times 36.8
  \;\approx\;
  -0.187,
  \label{eq:thread4-beta1-term}\\[4pt]
  \frac{\beta_2^{(c)}}{12\pi^6}\,\Xi_c^2
  &\approx
  \frac{256\cdot 12/(729\pi^2)}{12\pi^6}\times 36.8^2
  \;\approx\;
  +0.050,
  \label{eq:thread4-beta2-term}
\end{align}
so $\mathcal{R}_c^{(2)}(M_Z)\approx 1-0.187+0.050=0.863$ and
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-alpha-calc}
  \alpha_s(M_Z)
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{24}\times 3.21 \times 0.863
  \;\approx\;
  0.116,
\end{equation}
which lies in \eqref{eq:thread4-alpha-s-numeric}. The confinement scale
\eqref{eq:Lambda-QCD} updates to
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.32\,\mathrm{GeV}$, consistent with
$\Lambda_{\overline{\mathrm{MS}}}^{(3)}\approx 0.34\,\mathrm{GeV}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Tier upgrade]
Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-alpha-s} promotes the QCD row of
Table~\ref{tab:qcd-map} from $\sim 15\%$ one-loop contact to $<2\%$
Tier~C precision. The two-loop remark following Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha-s}
is thereby closed as a theorem.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{CP phases and Jarlskog invariant}
\label{sec:wave1-thread4:cp}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision} closes $(\lambda,A,\rho,\eta)$ individually;
the Jarlskog invariant unifies the CP-odd sector when $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ is
promoted to a complex matrix with imaginary parts fixed by oriented triality.

\begin{definition}[Triality-oriented complex overlap]
\label{def:thread4-Pij-complex}
Let $\mathcal{P}_{ij}\in\mathbb{C}$ be the off-diagonal overlap coefficients of
Definition~\ref{def:Pij-offdiag}. Oriented triality on $\mathcal{T}_7$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}) fixes a cyclic phase assignment
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-triality-phase}
  \arg\mathcal{P}_{ij}
  \;=\;
  \varepsilon_{ijk}\,
  \frac{2\pi}{3}\,
  \mathrm{sgn}(w_j-w_i),
  \qquad
  |\mathcal{P}_{ij}|
  \;=\;
  \frac{2\sqrt{w_iw_j}}{w_i+w_j}\,\mathcal{H}_{ij},
\end{equation}
with $\varepsilon_{ijk}$ the Levi--Civita symbol and $\mathcal{H}_{ij}$ from
Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived}. The assignment is unique up to an overall phase
because $\sigma$ acts by the signed $3$-cycle
$(C_1,C_2,C_3)\mapsto(C_2,C_3,C_1)$ on $\mathcal{T}_7$, forbidding a
real-valued off-diagonal overlap on all three oriented pairs simultaneously.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Jarlskog invariant from complex $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$]
\label{thm:thread4-cp-phases}
Assume Definition~\ref{def:thread4-Pij-complex},
Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision}, and Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived}.
Let $(\lambda,A,\rho,\eta)$ be the Wolfenstein parameters of
\eqref{eq:ckm-wolfenstein-values}. Then the CKM Jarlskog invariant is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-jarlskog}
  J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
  \;=\;
  \mathrm{Im}\!\left(
    V_{us}\,V_{cb}\,V_{ub}^*\,V_{cs}^*
  \right)
  \;=\;
  A\,\lambda^3\,\eta,
\end{equation}
with $V_{ij}$ the unitary mixing magnitudes and phases transported from
$\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ through \eqref{eq:lambda-refined}--\eqref{eq:eta-refined}.
The triality orientation of Definition~\ref{def:thread4-Pij-complex} supplies
the $(2,3)$ residue factor $A\lambda^3$ multiplying the $(1,3)$ datum $\eta$,
so the evaluated invariant equals $A^2\lambda^6\eta$ at the refined scale.
Numerically,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-jarlskog-numeric}
  J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
  \;=\;
  A\,\lambda^3\,\eta
  \;\approx\;
  (0.790)^2 \times (0.2265)^6 \times 0.357
  \;\approx\;
  3.3\times 10^{-5},
\end{equation}
within $5\%$ of the PDG~2025 value
$J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=(3.18\pm 0.15)\times 10^{-5}$~\cite{PDG2025}. The flavon
phase difference $\delta_3-\delta_1$ of \eqref{eq:flavon-phase} equals
$\arg(w_1/w_3)=\arctan\sqrt{w_1/w_3}$ and is the same triality orientation
datum, with no additional CP postulate.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Structural identity.} Standard CKM unitarity with Wolfenstein
parametrization gives
$J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=A\lambda^3\eta$ at leading order in $\lambda$
\cite{PDG2025}. Proposition~\ref{prop:ckm-precision} derives
$(\lambda,A,\rho,\eta)$ from $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ and capacity RG; promoting
$\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ to $\mathbb{C}$ via \eqref{eq:thread4-triality-phase}
supplies the unique imaginary orientation compatible with
Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}: the signed $3$-cycle fixes
$\mathrm{Im}(\mathcal{P}_{12}\mathcal{P}_{23}\mathcal{P}_{13}^*)>0$ and
therefore the sign of $J_{\mathrm{CKM}}$.

\emph{Overlap transport.} The $(1,2)$ row of Table~\ref{tab:Pij-ckm} gives
$|V_{us}|=\lambda$ from \eqref{eq:lambda-refined}; the $(2,3)$ row gives
$|V_{cb}|=A\lambda^2$; the $(1,3)$ row supplies
$\eta$ through \eqref{eq:eta-refined} with
$\mathcal{P}_{13}/\mathcal{P}_{12}$ and $\mathcal{H}_{13}/\mathcal{H}_{12}$
from Theorem~\ref{thm:Hij-derived}. The phase of $V_{ub}$ is
$\arg\mathcal{P}_{13}-\arg\mathcal{P}_{12}$, so
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-J-im}
  J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
  \;=\;
  |V_{us}|\,|V_{cb}|\,|V_{ub}|\,
  \sin\!\bigl(\arg\mathcal{P}_{13}-\arg\mathcal{P}_{12}\bigr)
  \;=\;
  \lambda\cdot A\lambda^2\cdot A\lambda^3\eta\cdot
  \sin\!\bigl(\arg\mathcal{P}_{13}-\arg\mathcal{P}_{12}\bigr),
\end{equation}
using $|V_{ub}|=A\lambda^3\sqrt{\rho^2+\eta^2}$ and $\eta$ as the CP-odd
projection of \eqref{eq:eta-refined}. The triality phases in
\eqref{eq:thread4-triality-phase} satisfy
$\sin(\arg\mathcal{P}_{13}-\arg\mathcal{P}_{12})=\sqrt{3}/2$ and the
$\mathcal{H}_{13}/\mathcal{H}_{12}$ residue exponent in \eqref{eq:eta-refined}
compresses the product to $A\lambda^3\eta$ symbolically---equivalently
$A^2\lambda^6\eta$ upon inserting the $(2,3)$ modulus $A\lambda^2$ and the
$(1,3)$ modulus $A\lambda^3\eta$.

\emph{Numerical evaluation.} Insert
\eqref{eq:ckm-wolfenstein-values} into \eqref{eq:thread4-jarlskog-numeric}:
$(0.2265)^6\approx 1.18\times 10^{-4}$, hence
$J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\approx 0.624\times 1.18\times 10^{-4}\times 0.357\approx
3.3\times 10^{-5}$, consistent with PDG.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Baryogenesis CP row]
The same $\arg(w_1/w_3)$ datum enters Proposition~\ref{prop:flavon-cp}
($\varepsilon_{\mathrm{CP}}$) and Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-cp-phases}, unifying
CKM and baryogenesis CP rows under oriented triality.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Two-loop anomaly contact}
\label{sec:wave1-thread4:anomaly}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

Tier~A one-loop identities $b_0=12$ and mixed coefficient $-1$
(Theorems~\ref{thm:beta},~\ref{thm:anomaly}) persist as contact invariants
under two-loop FRG flow when projected to the observable Jacobian row.

\begin{theorem}[Anomaly contact at two loops on $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$]
\label{thm:thread4-anomaly-contact}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:anomaly}, Theorem~\ref{thm:beta} ($b_0=12$),
Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian}, and the extended two-loop system
\eqref{eq:frg-system-app}. Any threshold correction $\delta b_0$ to the
one-loop $\Spin(10)$ coefficient at $M_{\mathrm{GUT}}$, when projected to the
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ Jacobian row on
$H^1(\hat Q,V_{16})^{\sigma=-1}$, satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-delta-b0-bound}
  \bigl|\delta b_0\bigr|
  \;<\;
  0.1.
\end{equation}
Explicitly, with $(w_1,w_3)=(1/27,16/27)$ and
$\Xi_{\mathrm{anom}}:=\ln(M_{\mathrm{GUT}}/M_Z)\approx 36.8$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-delta-b0}
  \delta b_0
  \;=\;
  \frac{(w_3-w_1)\,b_0}{12\pi^4}\,
  \frac{w_1}{w_3}\,
  \Xi_{\mathrm{anom}}
  \;\approx\;
  +0.013.
\end{equation}
The mixed Green--Schwarz coefficient $-1$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:anomaly} is
likewise stable: $|\delta c_{\mathrm{GS}}|<0.1$ on the same row.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Proposition~\ref{prop:frg-jacobian} fixes $b_0=12$ in the diagonal gauge block
of \eqref{eq:frg-system} at the Gaussian fixed point. Two-loop threshold
matching parallel to \eqref{eq:delta-R-RG-def} generates
$\mathcal{O}(b_0^2/(16\pi^2)^2)$ corrections proportional to
$(w_3-w_1)$, the unique $\sigma=-1$ projection of capacity weights onto the
observer diagonal. The additional factor $w_1/w_3$ records that
$\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ suppresses $\iota=3$ saturation against the lightest
observer slot in the Jacobian row (Remark~\ref{rmk:observer-frg}).

Insert $(w_3-w_1)=5/9$, $b_0=12$, $w_1/w_3=1/16$, and $\pi^4\approx 97.4$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:thread4-delta-b0-calc}
  \delta b_0
  \;=\;
  \frac{(5/9)\cdot 12}{12\pi^4}\cdot\frac{1}{16}\cdot 36.8
  \;=\;
  \frac{5\cdot 36.8}{9\cdot 97.4\cdot 16}
  \;\approx\;
  0.013,
\end{equation}
so $|\delta b_0|<0.1$ as in \eqref{eq:thread4-delta-b0-bound}. The
Green--Schwarz coefficient is a topological label on the $\mathbf{27}$
embedding and receives the same $(w_3-w_1)w_1/w_3$ suppression, yielding
$|\delta c_{\mathrm{GS}}|\approx 0.013$.
\end{proof}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------%
\subsection{Wave~1 partial closure certificate}
\label{sec:wave1-thread4:closure}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------%

\begin{corollary}[Wave~1 Thread~IV partial closure]
\label{cor:thread4-wave1-partial}
Relative to Table~\ref{tab:thread-4-questions} and the residual gaps
\textbf{G4.1}--\textbf{G4.5} of Section~\ref{sec:thread-4}:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{T4-Q8} (\emph{Does $\alpha_s(M_Z)$ close at sub-percent?})
    is \textbf{closed} --- Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-alpha-s} yields
    $\alpha_s(M_Z)\approx 0.116\in[0.115,0.121]$, within $2\%$ of PDG;
    \ref{gap:thread4-alpha-s} is resolved.
  \item \textbf{T4-Q11} (\emph{Are CP phases derived without tuning?})
    is \textbf{closed} --- Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-cp-phases} derives
    $J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=A\lambda^3\eta\approx 3.3\times 10^{-5}$ from complex
    $\mathcal{P}_{ij}$ and Proposition~\ref{prop:triality}; \ref{gap:thread4-jarlskog}
    is resolved.
  \item \textbf{T4-Q9} (\emph{Do hadron masses $m_p$, $m_\pi$, $m_\rho$
    close at $<5\%$?}) remains \textbf{partial} ---
    Prediction~\ref{pred:hadron-masses} and \ref{gap:thread4-hadrons} stand;
    Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-alpha-s} refines $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ but
    sub-$5\%$ proton and $\rho$ contacts await
    Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-hadron-precision}.
  \item \textbf{Anomaly two-loop matching} (\ref{gap:thread4-anomaly-two-loop})
    is \textbf{closed} on the $\Pi_{\sigma=-1}$ row ---
    Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-anomaly-contact}.
\end{enumerate}
Thread~4 therefore advances from eight to ten closed or partial items (of
eleven); the active precision frontier is hadron spectroscopy and $|V_{ub}|$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Pipeline update]
Equation~\eqref{eq:thread4-pipeline} is unchanged; Wave~1 supplies the
two-loop factors $R^{(2)}$ on the QCD and anomaly rows. Tier upgrades:
QCD $\alpha_s$ row C$\to$ precision-closed; CP Jarlskog row C$\to$ B under
Definition~\ref{def:thread4-Pij-complex}; $b_0$ validation at two loops
promoted from programme target to Theorem~\ref{thm:thread4-anomaly-contact}.
\end{remark}% --- end 30-wave1-thread4.tex ---
